     1	# Local transfer error telemetry (design)
     2	
     3	**Status**: Draft
     4	**Created**: 2026-07-06
     5	**Supersedes**: nothing
     6	**Decision ref**: pending ŌĆö Q1-Q4 owner-confirmed 2026-07-06 (folded into
     7	this doc below); Q5 (DraftŌåÆActive gate vs. D-2026-07-05-4) pending final
     8	confirmation, see bottom.
     9	
    10	**Held, not queued (pending confirmation)**: `docs/STATE.md`'s Queue is
    11	pinned to ONE_TRANSFER_PATH exclusively (**D-2026-07-05-4**, "the only work
    12	item until it ships"). The owner initially chose Draft-only/hold, then on
    13	review of these open questions said "we need to start collecting errors
    14	sooner than later to aid in dev" ŌĆö signaling urgency, but the exact
    15	mechanism (a recorded exception to D-2026-07-05-4 now vs. some other
    16	sequencing) still needs one explicit confirmation before this doc enters
    17	the Queue, flips Active, or any code lands (see **Q5** at the bottom).
    18	
    19	## Why this doc
    20	
    21	The owner hit the same hard-failure crash (`audit-17` ŌĆö a destination
    22	filesystem rejecting a `:` in a filename, `os error 22`) three times across
    23	two different USB drives while backing up `/home/michael/`, each time having
    24	to copy-paste the terminal error into chat. The ask: persist transfer
    25	failures locally so they can be reviewed as a batch ("sweep these all up")
    26	instead of by hand, per-crash ŌĆö specifically so a future Claude Code session
    27	can be told "address the errors in telemetry" and discover the full set
    28	itself, across whichever route each failure came from.
    29	
    30	Today's "telemetry" (`perf_history.rs` ŌåÆ `perf_local.jsonl`, read via
    31	`blit diagnostics perf`) only records **successful** transfers. Its schema
    32	has an `error_count` field, but every writer hardcodes it to `0`
    33	(`engine/history.rs`, `auto_tune/mod.rs`, `perf_predictor.rs`,
    34	`engine/tuning.rs`) ŌĆö dead. Worse, `record_performance_history` is only
    35	reached from the success path inside `run_local_mirror` (`engine/mod.rs:220,
    36	277, 314, 350, 792`, `engine/single_file.rs:42`); a top-level `Err` (exactly
    37	the `os error 22` case) writes nothing. Hard failures leave zero trace
    38	on disk today.
    39	
    40	## Goal
    41	
    42	Any `blit copy`/`mirror` invocation ŌĆö local, remote-mediated push/pull, or
    43	relayed/delegated remoteŌåÆremote ŌĆö that returns a top-level `Err` appends one
    44	record (timestamp, command shape, which route it took, and the full error
    45	chain already printed to stderr) to a new local, **uncapped** JSONL file. A
    46	new `blit diagnostics errors` verb lists those records (most-recent-first,
    47	`--limit`, `--json`, `--clear`), so the owner (or an agent session told to
    48	"address the errors in telemetry") can discover the full accumulated set
    49	without re-running commands or pasting terminal output.
    50	
    51	## Decisions (owner-confirmed 2026-07-06)
    52	
    53	These were open questions in the reviewed draft; the owner has answered all
    54	four, so they're stated here as settled, not open:
    55	
    56	- **Dedicated file** (was Q1): `errors_local.jsonl` is a new sibling file to
    57	  `perf_local.jsonl`, not a schema change to it.
    58	- **Message-chain only for v1** (was Q2): ship `error_chain` (the `eyre`
    59	  frame list) without `error_location` for the first slice; add
    60	  `error_location` capture later only if the `eyre`/`color_eyre` API allows
    61	  it without restructuring `color_eyre::install()`.
    62	- **Both local and remote-mediated routes** (was Q3): the owner wants one
    63	  place that "sees them all" regardless of route ŌĆö so this now covers every
    64	  `TransferRoute` the CLI's `run_transfer` observes (`LocalToLocal`,
    65	  `LocalToRemote`, `RemoteToLocal`, `RemoteToRemoteRelay`,
    66	  `RemoteToRemoteDelegated`), for every arm that runs to completion inline.
    67	  **Correction (codex v2 review, Medium)**: the first pass at this
    68	  paragraph claimed no arm ever takes a fire-and-forget path ŌĆö false.
    69	  `RemoteToRemoteDelegated` honors `--detach`
    70	  (`transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs:130-152`): with `args.detach` set,
    71	  the CLI returns a synthesized `Ok` as soon as the daemon confirms
    72	  `Started`, and the actual transfer continues on the daemon independently
    73	  ŌĆö a post-Started failure never reaches `run_transfer`'s `Result` at all,
    74	  detached or not. **Scope, corrected**: this plan covers every route's
    75	  failure *up to the point the CLI stops observing it* ŌĆö which is "the
    76	  whole thing" for `LocalToLocal`/`LocalToRemote`/`RemoteToLocal`/
    77	  `RemoteToRemoteRelay`, and "up to a successful `Started`" for a
    78	  `--detach`ed `RemoteToRemoteDelegated` transfer. A post-detach failure is
    79	  explicitly out of scope (same boundary as the daemon's own
    80	  `recents.jsonl`, which does cover it ŌĆö see below), not a gap this plan
    81	  claims to close. This does **not** mean merging with the daemon's own
    82	  `recents.jsonl` (`blit-daemon/src/recents_store.rs`) ŌĆö that stays the
    83	  separate mechanism for what the *daemon* observes independent of the
    84	  client (including everything past a detach); this plan only ever records
    85	  what the CLI process itself sees returned from `run_transfer`.
    86	- **No cap, for now** (was Q4): `errors_local.jsonl` is explicitly
    87	  **unbounded** during this development phase ŌĆö the owner clears it
    88	  manually (`--clear`) once the bugs it names are addressed. This is stated
    89	  as a deliberately temporary posture: **a follow-up slice** (not part of
    90	  this plan's initial slices) will make the whole feature **config-gated
    91	  opt-in** (mirroring `perf_history`'s `--enable`/`--disable`/
    92	  `options.perf_history` pattern) once it graduates past active development
    93	  use. Recording is **on by default, unconditionally**, for this phase ŌĆö
    94	  no new CLI flag or config toggle in the initial slices.
    95	
    96	## Non-goals
    97	
    98	- **Does not fix `audit-17`/`audit-18` themselves.** Those stay separate
    99	  TODO.md findings with their own owner design call (skip-and-report vs.
   100	  sanitize vs. clean fail-fast). This plan makes failures *durable and
   101	  reviewable*; it does not change transfer behavior on failure.
   102	- **Does not build a fault-kind taxonomy** (permission-denied / ENOSPC /
   103	  invalid-name / etc. as a structured enum). That's adjacent to the
   104	  deferred `F15` structured-logging epic (`TODO.md`). This plan persists the
   105	  raw `eyre` error-chain text, not a classified error type.
   106	- **Does not merge with the daemon's `recents.jsonl`** ŌĆö see Decisions
   107	  above. Covers CLI-observed failures only, across every route `run_transfer`
   108	  dispatches ŌĆö **except** a `--detach`ed `RemoteToRemoteDelegated` transfer
   109	  past its `Started` confirmation, which the CLI never observes (see
   110	  Decisions ŌĆö Q3 correction) and which stays exclusively the daemon
   111	  `recents.jsonl`'s job to record.
   112	- **`Commands::Move` and admin verbs (`scan`/`ls`/`du`/`df`/`rm`/`find`/
   113	  etc.) are out of scope for the initial slices** ŌĆö `Commands::Move` calls
   114	  a separate `run_move` function, not `run_transfer`; folding it in is a
   115	  candidate follow-up, not assumed here.
   116	- **No network transmission of any kind.** Fully local, on-device, same
   117	  trust model as `perf_local.jsonl` ŌĆö this is a diagnostic log the owner
   118	  (or an agent working locally) reads with a CLI verb, never phoned home.
   119	- **No automatic remediation** (retry-with-sanitized-name, skip-and-continue,
   120	  etc.) ŌĆö that's `audit-17`'s decision, not this plan's.
   121	- **No config-gated opt-in in the initial slices** ŌĆö see Decisions above;
   122	  deferred to a follow-up once this leaves active-development use.
   123	
   124	## Constraints
   125	
   126	- Local-only, on-device storage (matches `perf_local.jsonl`'s trust model ŌĆö
   127	  a backup tool must not silently exfiltrate path/filename data).
   128	- Append-only JSONL, **no size cap for now** (see Decisions ŌĆö Q4). The
   129	  owner clears it manually via `--clear`; a cap/rotation policy is deferred
   130	  to the future config-gated-opt-in slice, not this pass.
   131	- Must not slow down the hot (success) path ŌĆö the write happens once, on
   132	  the already-exceptional error/abort path, at process exit.
   133	- Cross-platform: reuses `blit_core::config::config_dir()`, already
   134	  cross-platform (`directories::ProjectDirs`). No new platform-specific
   135	  code needed.
   136	- The recorder itself must be failure-tolerant: a broken/unwritable config
   137	  dir must never mask or replace the original error ŌĆö recording is
   138	  best-effort, silent by default (matching `engine/history.rs`'s existing
   139	  `--verbose`-gated `eprintln!` convention for `perf_local.jsonl` write
   140	  failures, not the `log` facade ŌĆö see Design), around the real `Result`
   141	  that still propagates to the process exit code and stderr exactly as
   142	  today.
   143	
   144	## Acceptance criteria
   145	
   146	- [ ] Any `blit copy`/`mirror` invocation whose top-level result is `Err` ŌĆö
   147	      regardless of `TransferRoute` (local, remote-mediated, relayed,
   148	      delegated) ŌĆö appends exactly one record to a new local JSONL file
   149	      before the process exits, containing at minimum: schema_version,
   150	      timestamp, mode (Copy/Mirror), route (`None` if the failure predates
   151	      route selection), source root, dest root, and the error chain (every
   152	      `eyre` context frame's message, same content already printed to
   153	      stderr by `color_eyre`). **Exception**: a `--detach`ed
   154	      `RemoteToRemoteDelegated` transfer that reaches `Started` is a
   155	      success from the CLI's point of view (see Decisions ŌĆö Q3
   156	      correction) ŌĆö nothing to record; any failure after that point is
   157	      the daemon `recents.jsonl`'s job, not this file's.
   158	- [ ] `blit diagnostics errors [--limit N] [--json] [--clear]` reads the
   159	      file back, newest-first, mirroring `blit diagnostics perf`'s flag
   160	      conventions.
   161	- [ ] The file has **no size cap** in this pass ŌĆö verify it is *not*
   162	      rotated/truncated automatically; only `--clear` empties it.
   163	- [ ] `perf_local.jsonl` and its reader/predictor are completely unaffected
   164	      ŌĆö this is an additive, separate file, not a schema change to the
   165	      existing one.
   166	- [ ] Recording is unconditional (on by default) ŌĆö no new flag/config gate
   167	      in this pass.
   168	- [ ] Process exit code and stderr output for a failing command are
   169	      **byte-identical** to today's ŌĆö the recorder taps the `Result`, it
   170	      never changes what the user sees or the exit code.
   171	- [ ] A forced-failure integration test per route family (at least one
   172	      local-route failure and one remote-mediated-route failure) asserts a
   173	      record lands with the expected fields, including the correct `route`.
   174	- [ ] `cargo fmt`/`clippy`/`test --workspace` all green; test count does
   175	      not drop.
   176	
   177	## Design
   178	
   179	New module `blit-core/src/error_history.rs`, mirroring `perf_history.rs`'s
   180	shape (`FailureRecord` struct, `record_failure(...)`, `read_failures(limit)`,
   181	`clear_failures()`), writing to `errors_local.jsonl` in the same
   182	`config::config_dir()` as `perf_local.jsonl` ŌĆö a sibling file, not a shared
   183	schema.
   184	
   185	Draft schema (`FailureRecord`):
   186	- `schema_version: u32`
   187	- `timestamp` (same convention as `PerformanceRecord`)
   188	- `mode: TransferMode` (reuse the existing `Copy`/`Mirror` enum from
   189	  `perf_history.rs`)
   190	- `route: Option<String>` ŌĆö a plain string label (`"local_to_local"` /
   191	  `"local_to_remote"` / `"remote_to_local"` / `"remote_to_remote_relay"` /
   192	  `"remote_to_remote_delegated"`), `None` when the failure happened before
   193	  a route was ever selected (see Wiring ŌĆö codex v2 Medium finding on why
   194	  this is `Option`, not `String`).
   195	- `source: String`, `dest: String` (the two root paths/endpoints as given
   196	  on the CLI)
   197	- `error_chain: Vec<String>` ŌĆö each frame of the returned `eyre::Report`'s
   198	  `.chain()`, in order (outermost context first, root cause last) ŌĆö the
   199	  same information `color_eyre` prints as the numbered `0:`/`1:`/... list,
   200	  captured programmatically instead of scraped from stderr text.
   201	- `error_location: Option<String>` ŌĆö always `None` in the first slice (see
   202	  Decisions ŌĆö Q2); a later slice may populate it.
   203	
   204	**Wiring** ŌĆö a single chokepoint in `crates/blit-cli/src/main.rs`'s
   205	`Commands::Copy`/`Commands::Mirror` arms, wrapping
   206	`run_with_retries(..., || run_transfer(...)).await` to bind the `Result`
   207	before it returns, call `error_history::record_failure(...)` when it's
   208	`Err`, then propagate the *original, untouched* `Result` unchanged. This
   209	one point naturally covers every `TransferRoute`, matching the owner's
   210	"both" answer (Q3) ŌĆö no need to instrument each of the five route arms
   211	individually.
   212	
   213	**`route` derivation ŌĆö corrected** (codex v2 Medium finding: the first
   214	pass at this section hand-waved "re-derive it from `args`/
   215	`select_transfer_route` inside the recorder" ŌĆö but `error_history` lives in
   216	`blit-core`, and `TransferRoute`/`select_transfer_route` live in
   217	`blit-app::transfers::dispatch` (`dispatch.rs:69,112`), a layer *above*
   218	`blit-core` in this workspace's dependency direction; `blit-core` cannot
   219	depend on `blit-app`. It also didn't address that `run_transfer` can fail
   220	before a route is ever selected, e.g. `parse_transfer_endpoint`/
   221	`build_filter_spec` failures ahead of the `match select_transfer_route`.).
   222	Fix: `error_history::record_failure` (in `blit-core`) takes a plain
   223	`route: Option<&str>` parameter ŌĆö it never imports or knows about
   224	`TransferRoute`. `run_transfer` (in `blit-cli`, which already sees
   225	`TransferRoute` since it matches on it directly) is the thing that knows
   226	which route it selected and whether it got there before failing; it needs
   227	a way to surface that alongside its `Result` up through
   228	`run_with_retries` to the `main.rs` chokepoint ŌĆö the concrete shape (e.g.
   229	`run_transfer` returning `Result<(), (Option<TransferRoute>, eyre::Report)>`,
   230	or a side-channel `Cell`/return wrapper) is implementation detail for
   231	slice 2, not pinned here, but it must exist in the `blit-cli`/`blit-app`
   232	layer and hand `error_history` only a stringified `Option<&str>`.
   233	
   234	*(History: an earlier draft of this doc scoped itself to local-only and, on
   235	codex review, was found to have wired the recorder at this exact same
   236	`main.rs` chokepoint ŌĆö which the reviewer correctly flagged as inconsistent
   237	with a **local-only** stated scope, since this chokepoint sees every route.
   238	The owner has since widened the stated scope to cover every route (Q3), so
   239	this chokepoint is now the right one for the (new) stated scope; the
   240	review's underlying point ŌĆö design and wiring must agree on scope ŌĆö still
   241	holds and is satisfied here.)*
   242	
   243	**Recorder-failure handling**: matches the existing precedent in
   244	`engine/history.rs::record_performance_history` (`history.rs:36-40`), which
   245	already solves this exact problem for `perf_local.jsonl` ŌĆö a failed history
   246	write is silently dropped unless `--verbose`, via a direct `eprintln!`
   247	gated on `options.verbose`, **not** the `log` facade (`blit` installs a
   248	real stderr backend for `log::warn!` in `stderr_log.rs`, so using it here
   249	would itself alter stderr on a recorder failure, breaking the
   250	byte-identical-stderr acceptance criterion above).
   251	
   252	New CLI verb: `blit diagnostics errors` alongside the existing
   253	`run_diagnostics_perf` in `crates/blit-cli/src/diagnostics.rs`, same flag
   254	shape (`--limit`, `--json`, `--clear`).
   255	
   256	## Slices
   257	
   258	1. **`error_history` module** ŌĆö schema (incl. `route`), `record_failure`/
   259	   `read_failures`/`clear_failures` (no cap/rotation ŌĆö see Decisions Q4),
   260	   unit tests (round-trip, tolerant read of a corrupted/partial last line ŌĆö
   261	   matching `perf_history.rs`'s existing tolerance).
   262	2. **Wire the `Commands::Copy`/`Commands::Mirror` arms** in `main.rs` to
   263	   call `record_failure` on `Err`, before propagating, unchanged exit
   264	   code/stderr; thread `Option<TransferRoute>` out of `run_transfer`
   265	   (shape TBD in-slice, see Design) so the chokepoint can stringify it for
   266	   `record_failure`'s `route` parameter without `blit-core` ever seeing
   267	   `TransferRoute`. Integration tests: force a local-route failure (e.g.
   268	   destination path that can't be created) and, separately, a
   269	   remote-mediated-route failure (e.g. an unreachable daemon endpoint);
   270	   assert each lands exactly one record with the expected
   271	   `source`/`dest`/`mode`/`route`/non-empty `error_chain`; a third forces a
   272	   pre-route-selection failure (e.g. an unparseable endpoint) and asserts
   273	   the record lands with `route: None`; a fourth runs a `--detach`ed
   274	   `RemoteToRemoteDelegated` transfer to a successful `Started` and asserts
   275	   **no** record lands (it's a CLI-observed success, per Decisions ŌĆö Q3
   276	   correction); assert stderr/exit-code parity with the no-recorder
   277	   baseline throughout.
   278	3. **`blit diagnostics errors` read-back verb** ŌĆö list/limit/json/clear,
   279	   unit + CLI-level tests.
   280	
   281	Deliberately **not** a slice here (future follow-ups, owner-gated):
   282	folding `Move`/admin verbs into the same recorder; capturing
   283	`error_location` if a clean API surface exists (Q2); config-gated opt-in
   284	(Q4 follow-up) with a size cap once that lands; any interaction with
   285	`audit-17`'s eventual skip-and-report behavior, where a partially-successful
   286	transfer with per-file skips might also want a record here ŌĆö that's a
   287	follow-up once `audit-17` itself is designed, not this plan's job.
   288	
   289	## Q5 ŌĆö resolved 2026-07-06: timing vs. D-2026-07-05-4
   290	
   291	Asked the owner directly: given **D-2026-07-05-4** ("ONE_TRANSFER_PATH ŌĆö
   292	the only work item until it ships") is worded in absolute terms, and given
   293	the owner also wants error collection started "sooner than later to aid in
   294	dev," which of two mechanisms should apply ŌĆö
   295	
   296	- **(a) Explicit, recorded exception, start now**: a new `D-2026-07-06-n`
   297	  decision carving out this specific exception, this plan added to
   298	  `docs/STATE.md`'s Queue, flipped `**Status**: Draft` ŌåÆ `Active`, slice 1
   299	  begun in parallel with otp-7; or
   300	- **(b) Next natural pause**: no new decision recorded, no Queue entry ŌĆö
   301	  pick this up the moment the current otp-7 slice reaches a stopping point.
   302	
   303	**Owner chose (b).** Recorded as a timing note in `docs/STATE.md`'s Open
   304	Questions (not the Queue), so it survives past this session without
   305	touching D-2026-07-05-4's text.
   306	
   307	**Acknowledged tension (codex v2 review, Low, correctly caught)**: option
   308	(b) as worded ŌĆö "without formally reopening" D-2026-07-05-4 ŌĆö doesn't
   309	actually dissolve the conflict with that decision's absolute wording ("the
   310	**only** work item until it ships"); starting this plan's slice 1 before
   311	ONE_TRANSFER_PATH ships is, in substance, an exception to it regardless of
   312	whether a `D-2026-07-06-n` entry gets written. This doc does not pretend
   313	otherwise. The owner's choice stands as an explicit, informed, small-scope
   314	call made with that tension stated plainly in front of them (this section,
   315	and the live back-and-forth that produced it) ŌĆö not a silent override
   316	inferred from ambiguous wording, which is what AGENTS.md's conflict-flagging
   317	principle actually guards against. If a future reader wants this made fully
   318	rigorous, the clean fix is to record a real (if lightweight)
   319	`D-2026-07-06-n` ŌĆö "informal pause-point exception to D-2026-07-05-4 for
   320	LOCAL_ERROR_TELEMETRY.md, owner-approved 2026-07-06" ŌĆö the moment this
   321	plan actually flips Active, rather than leaving the exception undocumented
   322	in `DECISIONS.md` indefinitely.

   106	- [x] **audit-14** Redundant `seek` system calls in sequential block-level resume copies.

   109	### New audit findings (2026-07-06)
   110	
   111	- [ ] **audit-16** `spawn_manifest_task`'s "Enumerated N entriesŌĆ” (streaming
   112	      manifest)" heartbeat (`crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:114-183`)
   113	      prints unconditionally on a 1s wall-clock timer ŌĆö no `--verbose` gate.
   114	      `docs/plan/LOCAL_TRANSFER_HEURISTICS.md:42` (Status: Historical)
   115	      documents the original intent as verbose-gated ("`--verbose` shows
   116	      real-time heartbeat messagesŌĆ” Default mode remains quiet unless a
   117	      stall occurs"); the shipped code never wired that check in, so every
   118	      `copy`/`mirror` run spams the heartbeat regardless of verbosity ŌĆö local
   119	      mirror hits this same manifest-scan path too, per
   120	      `engine/strategy.rs:81` (mirror/checksum/force-tar always take the
   121	      streaming path, which is unified with remote push). Fix: gate the
   122	      print in `spawn_manifest_task` behind the caller's verbose option
   123	      (the function has no visibility into CLI args today ŌĆö thread a flag
   124	      through `LocalMirrorOptions`/the equivalent remote-push options).
   125	      Related, already filed, do not re-file: `--progress` (`-p`)
   126	      auto-enabling on TTY regardless of the flag is
   127	      `docs/audit/findings/drift-principles.md`
   128	      (`drift-spinner-vs-quiet-default-decision-conflict`).
   129	- [ ] **audit-17** Local `copy` aborts the entire transfer on one
   130	      filename the destination filesystem rejects, instead of
   131	      skipping/warning and continuing. Reported: `blit copy
   132	      /home/michael/ /run/media/michael/8247-7E92/michael -ypv`
   133	      failed enumerating ~88k entries in, at
   134	      `crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:605`
   135	      (`write_tar_shard_payload`'s parallel-write closure) ŌĆö
   136	      `std::fs::create_dir_all` on a NuGet http-cache path whose
   137	      final component is `670c1461c...$ps:_api.nuget.org_v3_index.json`
   138	      returned `Invalid argument (os error 22)`. The source filename
   139	      is valid on the source (Linux/ext4) fs but contains a `:`,
   140	      which is illegal on FAT/exFAT/NTFS-strict destinations.
   141	      *Assumption, unverified ŌĆö drive wasn't mounted to confirm:*
   142	      the destination (`/run/media/...`, hex volume label
   143	      `8247-7E92`, the classic Linux label format for an
   144	      unlabeled FAT-family volume) is exFAT or FAT32. Grepped
   145	      `crates/blit-core/src` for existing invalid-filename handling
   146	      (`os error 22`, `sanitize_name`, `illegal.*char`, etc.) ŌĆö none
   147	      found; this is a real gap, not a regression. One bad name
   148	      currently kills the whole run rather than being
   149	      skipped/reported/renamed. Fix needs a design call (owner
   150	      input required, `plan` this before coding): per-file
   151	      skip-and-report vs. optional name-sanitization vs. fail-fast
   152	      with a clear top-level error instead of a raw `os error 22` +
   153	      internal path/line. Whatever is chosen must apply uniformly
   154	      to both the local-mirror and remote tar-shard receive paths
   155	      (same `write_tar_shard_payload` helper backs both, per
   156	      audit-16 above). **Confirmed reproducible**: identical failure
   157	      (same path, same error, same line, same ~88129-entry offset)
   158	      recurred verbatim on a second run targeting a different mount
   159	      (`/run/media/michael/USB_DRIVE/michael`) ŌĆö not a one-off fluke;
   160	      the FAT-family-destination assumption above is now corroborated
   161	      by a second independent mount exhibiting the same `:`-rejection.
   162	      **Second manifestation, same closure, one line down**: after
   163	      that NuGet-cache directory issue was worked past (retried on a
   164	      cleared destination), the identical `os error 22` recurred at
   165	      `sink.rs:608` ŌĆö this time `std::fs::write` on a regular file
   166	      whose name is `frostfell06.dds:crc` (unrelated content, a game
   167	      asset tree, not NuGet). Confirms the bug is general to any path
   168	      component containing an illegal character, not create_dir_all-
   169	      specific or NuGet-cache-specific ŌĆö the fix must cover both the
   170	      `create_dir_all` (line 605) and `write` (line 608) call sites in
   171	      the same closure (and their mirror in the local-mirror path, per
   172	      the note above).
   173	- [ ] **audit-18** Non-UTF-8 source filenames are silently corrupted
   174	      during enumeration, then fail to open, aborting the whole
   175	      transfer. Reported: `blit copy /home/michael/
   176	      /run/media/michael/USB_DRIVE/michael -ypv` (same host as
   177	      audit-17, later re-run) failed ~377k entries in at
   178	      `crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:360`
   179	      (`build_tar_shard`'s `std::fs::File::open(&full_path)`) with
   180	      `No such file or directory (os error 2)` opening
   181	      `.../Claudia-by-Choice-codex_1.0<U+FFFD>` ŌĆö the trailing
   182	      replacement character is the tell. Root cause:
   183	      `crate::path_posix::relative_path_to_posix` (`path_posix.rs:36-44`)
   184	      builds the canonical relative-path `String` with
   185	      `c.as_os_str().to_string_lossy()` per component ŌĆö on Linux/ext4
   186	      a filename can be any non-`/`/non-NUL byte sequence, and a
   187	      non-UTF-8 one gets its invalid bytes replaced with U+FFFD
   188	      *irreversibly*. `build_tar_shard` then does
   189	      `source_root.join(rel)` on that corrupted string, which no
   190	      longer names the real file ŌåÆ `ENOENT`. `FileEntry.path` itself
   191	      (`fs_enum.rs:14`) is a real `PathBuf` (exact bytes preserved),
   192	      so the corruption happens specifically at the `PathBuf ŌåÆ String`
   193	      relative-path conversion, not at enumeration. `relative_path_to_posix`
   194	      is the single canonical helper for this and is called from
   195	      `engine/mirror.rs`, `mirror_planner.rs`, `remote/transfer/{payload,tar_safety}.rs`,
   196	      `remote/endpoint.rs`, and `remote/push/client/helpers.rs` ŌĆö i.e.
   197	      local mirror and remote push both go through the lossy path, so
   198	      this isn't a remote-only/proto-only constraint. Fix needs a
   199	      design call (owner input required, `plan` this before coding):
   200	      the wire `FileHeader.relative_path`/`FileBlock.relative_path`
   201	      fields are proto3 `string`, which is UTF-8-only at the gRPC
   202	      layer, so a full fix for the remote path needs an encoding
   203	      scheme that round-trips arbitrary bytes through a UTF-8-safe
   204	      string (e.g. percent-encode invalid bytes, or WTF-8) ŌĆö local
   205	      mirror has no such wire constraint and could preserve raw
   206	      `OsString`/`PathBuf` throughout instead. Same failure class as
   207	      audit-17 (one bad filename kills the entire run instead of
   208	      being skipped/reported) ŌĆö whatever skip/report/fail-fast
   209	      behavior gets designed for audit-17 should likely cover this
   210	      case too, but the root cause here is enumeration-side path
   211	      corruption, not destination-fs charset rejection, so treat as
   212	      a separate fix even if the error-handling policy ends up shared.
   213

     8	## F1 (High) ŌĆö proposed chokepoint records every route, not just local ŌĆö ACCEPTED
     9	
    10	**Codex**: the doc's first draft wired the failure recorder at
    11	`crates/blit-cli/src/main.rs`'s `Commands::Copy`/`Commands::Mirror` arms, but
    12	`run_transfer` (called from both) dispatches `LocalToLocal`/`LocalToRemote`/
    13	`RemoteToLocal`/`RemoteToRemoteRelay`/`RemoteToRemoteDelegated` from one function
    14	via `select_transfer_route` (`transfers/mod.rs:101-287`). Wiring at `main.rs` would
    15	record every route's failures, including remote ones and pre-dispatch argument
    16	bails, contradicting the doc's stated local-only scope.
    17	
    18	**Adjudication: ACCEPTED (real).** Verified by reading `transfers/mod.rs:101-287`:
    19	`run_transfer` is a single function whose `match select_transfer_route(...)` covers
    20	five route variants, each with its own `!src.exists()` bail before calling its
    21	route-specific runner. `main.rs`'s `Commands::Copy`/`Mirror` arms call
    22	`run_with_retries(..., || run_transfer(...)).await?` ŌĆö there is no route
    23	information left by the time an `Err` reaches that point. The proposed chokepoint
    24	was too high in the call stack for a local-only feature.
    25	
    26	**Fix**: relocated the chokepoint into `run_transfer`'s `TransferRoute::LocalToLocal`
    27	arm specifically (`transfers/mod.rs:235-241`) ŌĆö wraps that arm's
    28	`run_local_transfer(...)` call (and its local `!src.exists()` bail, in-scope since
    29	it's still a local-route failure), leaving every other route arm untouched. Added a
    30	slice-2 test requirement pinning that a non-`LocalToLocal` route failure does
    31	**not** produce a record.
    32	
    33	## F2 (Medium) ŌĆö recorder-failure handling contradicts byte-identical stderr ŌĆö ACCEPTED
    34	
    35	**Codex**: the doc said a recorder failure logs via `log::warn!`, but `blit`
    36	installs a real stderr backend for the `log` facade (`stderr_log.rs`, wired
    37	`main.rs:35`) that prints `blit: warn: <msg>` to stderr on every `log::warn!`. That
    38	would itself change stderr output when recording fails, contradicting the doc's own
    39	"process exit code and stderr output... byte-identical to today's" acceptance
    40	criterion.
    41	
    42	**Adjudication: ACCEPTED (real).** Verified `stderr_log.rs:24-32`: the installed
    43	`Log` impl unconditionally `eprintln!`s any enabled record. Found the existing
    44	precedent for exactly this problem: `engine/history.rs::record_performance_history`
    45	(lines 36-40) already solves it for `perf_local.jsonl` ŌĆö a failed history write is
    46	silently dropped unless `options.verbose`, via a direct `eprintln!` gated on the
    47	verbose flag, not the `log` facade.
    48	
    49	**Fix**: switched the design to match that existing convention ŌĆö silent by default,
    50	`--verbose`-gated `eprintln!`, so default-mode stderr is unaffected by a recorder
    51	failure either way.
    52

     8	## F1 (Medium) ŌĆö "no fire-and-forget/detached path" claim is false ŌĆö ACCEPTED
     9	
    10	**Codex**: `run_transfer` does await each `TransferRoute` arm inline, but the
    11	delegated route can take `--detach`: `run_remote_to_remote_direct` returns after
    12	`Started` and the daemon continues independently. Post-Started failures will not
    13	reach the `main.rs` wrapper.

    16	`transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs:130-152`: `DelegatedPullExecution.detach:
    17	args.detach`, and the `if args.detach { ... }` branch returns a synthesized
    18	zero-summary `Ok` as soon as the daemon confirms the `Started` event, dropping the
    19	receiver ŌĆö the transfer continues on the daemon with no CLI process attached. A
    20	failure after that point never produces an `Err` for `run_transfer` to return.
    21	
    22	**Fix**: scoped the doc precisely ŌĆö covers every route's failure up to the point
    23	the CLI stops observing it, which is the whole transfer for four of the five
    24	routes and "up to a successful `Started`" for a `--detach`ed
    25	`RemoteToRemoteDelegated` transfer. Added an explicit non-goal/acceptance-criteria
    26	exception and a slice-2 test asserting no record lands for a successfully detached
    27	transfer.
    28	
    29	## F2 (Medium) ŌĆö `route` field derivation hand-waved + crate-layering bug ŌĆö ACCEPTED
    30	
    31	**Codex**: a `blit-core::error_history` recorder cannot rederive route via
    32	`select_transfer_route` because that lives in `blit-app`; also `run_transfer` can
    33	fail before route selection/parsing succeeds. "Return the route alongside its
    34	Result" needs the API explicitly shaped to preserve `Option<Route>` through
    35	`run_with_retries`; as written this was hand-waved.
    36	
    37	**Adjudication: ACCEPTED (real).** Verified: `TransferRoute`/`select_transfer_route`
    38	are defined in `blit-app/src/transfers/dispatch.rs:69,112`; `blit-core` cannot
    39	depend on `blit-app` (wrong direction in this workspace's layering ŌĆö `blit-core` is
    40	the foundational library every other crate depends on, never the reverse). Also
    41	confirmed `run_transfer` has pre-route-selection fallible calls (e.g. endpoint
    42	parsing) before its `match select_transfer_route(...)`.
    43	
    44	**Fix**: `route` is now `Option<String>` ŌĆö a plain string label, `None` when the
    45	failure predates route selection. `error_history` (in `blit-core`) never imports
    46	or knows about `TransferRoute`; the stringification happens in `blit-cli`/
    47	`blit-app`, which already see the enum. Slice 2 now explicitly says
    48	`run_transfer` needs to thread `Option<TransferRoute>` out alongside its `Result`
    49	(exact shape left to the slice, but the crate-boundary constraint is now stated,
    50	not hand-waved), with tests for both the `None` case and the `--detach` exclusion.

The previous DEVLOG entry (2026-06-20 20:57:45Z) recorded REV3's "**two** static tables, not three; `push/control.rs::desired_streams` and `pull.rs::pull_stream_count` were stale" ŌĆö **that is incorrect** (correcting forward, since DEVLOG is append-only): all three ladders are live ŌĆö `remote/tuning.rs::determine_remote_tuning` (tuning.rs:11), `desired_streams` (`push/control.rs:476`, already file-count-aware), `pull_stream_count` (`pull.rs:904`) ŌĆö and `tuning.rs:7-10`'s own doc comment says "the daemon's push negotiation currently runs its own ladder and wins." v1's "three ladders" enumeration was substantially right.  ### New audit findings (2026-07-06)
 
 - [ ] **audit-16** `spawn_manifest_task`'s "Enumerated N entriesŌĆ” (streaming
       manifest)" heartbeat (`crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:114-183`)
       prints unconditionally on a 1s wall-clock timer ŌĆö no `--verbose` gate.
       `docs/plan/LOCAL_TRANSFER_HEURISTICS.md:42` (Status: Historical)
       documents the original intent as verbose-gated ("`--verbose` shows
       real-time heartbeat messagesŌĆ” Default mode remains quiet unless a
       stall occurs"); the shipped code never wired that check in, so every
       `copy`/`mirror` run spams the heartbeat regardless of verbosity ŌĆö local
       mirror hits this same manifest-scan path too, per
       `engine/strategy.rs:81` (mirror/checksum/force-tar always take the
       streaming path, which is unified with remote push). Fix: gate the
       print in `spawn_manifest_task` behind the caller's verbose option
       (the function has no visibility into CLI args today ŌĆö thread a flag
       through `LocalMirrorOptions`/the equivalent remote-push options).
       Related, already filed, do not re-file: `--progress` (`-p`)
       auto-enabling on TTY regardless of the flag is
       `docs/audit/findings/drift-principles.md`
       (`drift-spinner-vs-quiet-default-decision-conflict`).
+- [ ] **audit-17** Local `copy` aborts the entire transfer on one
+      filename the destination filesystem rejects, instead of
+      skipping/warning and continuing. Reported: `blit copy
+      /home/michael/ /run/media/michael/8247-7E92/michael -ypv`
+      failed enumerating ~88k entries in, at
+      `crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:605`
+      (`write_tar_shard_payload`'s parallel-write closure) ŌĆö
+      `std::fs::create_dir_all` on a NuGet http-cache path whose
+      final component is `670c1461c...$ps:_api.nuget.org_v3_index.json`
+      returned `Invalid argument (os error 22)`. The source filename
+      is valid on the source (Linux/ext4) fs but contains a `:`,
+      which is illegal on FAT/exFAT/NTFS-strict destinations.
+      *Assumption, unverified ŌĆö drive wasn't mounted to confirm:*
+      the destination (`/run/media/...`, hex volume label
+      `8247-7E92`, the classic Linux label format for an
+      unlabeled FAT-family volume) is exFAT or FAT32. Grepped
+      `crates/blit-core/src` for existing invalid-filename handling
+      (`os error 22`, `sanitize_name`, `illegal.*char`, etc.) ŌĆö none
+      found; this is a real gap, not a regression. One bad name
+      currently kills the whole run rather than being
+      skipped/reported/renamed. Fix needs a design call (owner
+      input required, `plan` this before coding): per-file
+      skip-and-report vs. optional name-sanitization vs. fail-fast
+      with a clear top-level error instead of a raw `os error 22` +
+      internal path/line. Whatever is chosen must apply uniformly
+      to both the local-mirror and remote tar-shard receive paths
+      (same `write_tar_shard_payload` helper backs both, per
+      audit-16 above). **Confirmed reproducible**: identical failure
+      (same path, same error, same line, same ~88129-entry offset)
+      recurred verbatim on a second run targeting a different mount
+      (`/run/media/michael/USB_DRIVE/michael`) ŌĆö not a one-off fluke;
+      the FAT-family-destination assumption above is now corroborated
+      by a second independent mount exhibiting the same `:`-rejection.
+      **Second manifestation, same closure, one line down**: after
+      that NuGet-cache directory issue was worked past (retried on a
+      cleared destination), the identical `os error 22` recurred at
+      `sink.rs:608` ŌĆö this time `std::fs::write` on a regular file
+      whose name is `frostfell06.dds:crc` (unrelated content, a game
+      asset tree, not NuGet). Confirms the bug is general to any path
+      component containing an illegal character, not create_dir_all-
+      specific or NuGet-cache-specific ŌĆö the fix must cover both the
+      `create_dir_all` (line 605) and `write` (line 608) call sites in
+      the same closure (and their mirror in the local-mirror path, per
+      the note above).
+- [ ] **audit-18** Non-UTF-8 source filenames are silently corrupted
+      during enumeration, then fail to open, aborting the whole
+      transfer. Reported: `blit copy /home/michael/
+      /run/media/michael/USB_DRIVE/michael -ypv` (same host as
+      audit-17, later re-run) failed ~377k entries in at
+      `crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:360`
+      (`build_tar_shard`'s `std::fs::File::open(&full_path)`) with
+      `No such file or directory (os error 2)` opening
+      `.../Claudia-by-Choice-codex_1.0<U+FFFD>` ŌĆö the trailing
+      replacement character is the tell. Root cause:
+      `crate::path_posix::relative_path_to_posix` (`path_posix.rs:36-44`)
+      builds the canonical relative-path `String` with
+      `c.as_os_str().to_string_lossy()` per component ŌĆö on Linux/ext4
+      a filename can be any non-`/`/non-NUL byte sequence, and a
+      non-UTF-8 one gets its invalid bytes replaced with U+FFFD
+      *irreversibly*. `build_tar_shard` then does
+      `source_root.join(rel)` on that corrupted string, which no
+      longer names the real file ŌåÆ `ENOENT`. `FileEntry.path` itself
+      (`fs_enum.rs:14`) is a real `PathBuf` (exact bytes preserved),
+      so the corruption happens specifically at the `PathBuf ŌåÆ String`
+      relative-path conversion, not at enumeration. `relative_path_to_posix`
+      is the single canonical helper for this and is called from
+      `engine/mirror.rs`, `mirror_planner.rs`, `remote/transfer/{payload,tar_safety}.rs`,
+      `remote/endpoint.rs`, and `remote/push/client/helpers.rs` ŌĆö i.e.
+      local mirror and remote push both go through the lossy path, so
+      this isn't a remote-only/proto-only constraint. Fix needs a
+      design call (owner input required, `plan` this before coding):
+      the wire `FileHeader.relative_path`/`FileBlock.relative_path`
+      fields are proto3 `string`, which is UTF-8-only at the gRPC
+      layer, so a full fix for the remote path needs an encoding
+      scheme that round-trips arbitrary bytes through a UTF-8-safe
+      string (e.g. percent-encode invalid bytes, or WTF-8) ŌĆö local
+      mirror has no such wire constraint and could preserve raw
+      `OsString`/`PathBuf` throughout instead. Same failure class as
+      audit-17 (one bad filename kills the entire run instead of
+      being skipped/reported) ŌĆö whatever skip/report/fail-fast
+      behavior gets designed for audit-17 should likely cover this
+      case too, but the root cause here is enumeration-side path
+      corruption, not destination-fs charset rejection, so treat as
+      a separate fix even if the error-handling policy ends up shared.

 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	//! Canonical POSIX-form rendering of relative paths for the wire /
     2	//! manifest layer.
     3	//!
     4	//! Every place blit converts a local `Path` (the OS filesystem walker's
     5	//! native representation) into the wire/manifest's forward-slash string
     6	//! form must route through [`relative_path_to_posix`].
     7	//!
     8	//! ## Why a helper, not a string `replace('\\', "/")`?
     9	//!
    10	//! Earlier code did `path.to_string_lossy().replace('\\', "/")` to
    11	//! convert Windows-native `\` separators to `/` for the wire. That works
    12	//! "by accident" on Windows but is **destructive on POSIX**, where `\`
    13	//! is a legal filename character (e.g. macOS apps like Logic Pro ship
    14	//! plug-in presets named `1\4 Single.pst`, with a literal backslash). A
    15	//! blanket string-`replace` rewrites that filename character to `/`,
    16	//! creating a phantom path component that doesn't exist on disk; the
    17	//! manifest lookup then misses and the transfer fails (`tar shard
    18	//! produced unexpected entry ŌĆ” (not in manifest)`).
    19	//!
    20	//! Walking [`Path::components`] is the right primitive: on Windows it
    21	//! splits on the native `\` (or `/`), on POSIX it splits on `/` only.
    22	//! Joining the resulting components with `/` produces the canonical
    23	//! POSIX form on every platform, and any literal `\` (or `:`, or other
    24	//! non-separator byte) inside a single component survives untouched.
    25	
    26	use std::path::Path;
    27	
    28	/// Render a relative `Path` as a forward-slash-joined POSIX-form string
    29	/// for the wire / manifest. Components are joined via
    30	/// [`Path::components`], so the result is correct on both POSIX (where
    31	/// `\` is a legal filename character) and Windows (where `\` is the
    32	/// native separator).
    33	///
    34	/// Empty paths and bare `.` produce an empty string ŌĆö the convention
    35	/// the daemon wire format uses for "the module root".
    36	pub fn relative_path_to_posix(path: &Path) -> String {
    37	    if path.as_os_str().is_empty() || path == Path::new(".") {
    38	        return String::new();
    39	    }
    40	    path.components()
    41	        .map(|c| c.as_os_str().to_string_lossy())
    42	        .collect::<Vec<_>>()
    43	        .join("/")
    44	}
    45	
    46	/// Render a relative path expressed as a string (e.g. user input or a
    47	/// wire-supplied value of unknown provenance) as canonical POSIX form,
    48	/// applying the same component-aware semantics as
    49	/// [`relative_path_to_posix`]. On Windows, a user-typed `Folder\file` is
    50	/// split on the native separator; on POSIX, `Folder\file` is a single
    51	/// filename component and is preserved verbatim.
    52	///
    53	/// **Trailing-separator semantics are preserved** because for user
    54	/// input the trailing separator is a meaningful UX signal ŌĆö "this
    55	/// prefix names a directory; complete *inside* it" (the rsync /
    56	/// shell-completion convention). `Path::components()` strips trailing
    57	/// separators, so we detect them on the raw input and re-attach a
    58	/// canonical `/` after the canonicalization. On POSIX a trailing
    59	/// backslash is **not** a separator (it's a literal filename byte) and
    60	/// stays as part of the last component; on Windows a trailing native
    61	/// `\` IS a separator and round-trips as `/`. Round-1 reopen
    62	/// (GPT review) ŌĆö `sub/` was canonicalizing to `sub`, which broke
    63	/// `split_completion_prefix`'s "list inside sub/" path.
    64	pub fn relative_str_to_posix(s: &str) -> String {
    65	    let trailing_sep = s
    66	        .chars()
    67	        .next_back()
    68	        .map(std::path::is_separator)
    69	        .unwrap_or(false);
    70	    let canonical = relative_path_to_posix(Path::new(s));
    71	    if trailing_sep && !canonical.is_empty() && !canonical.ends_with('/') {
    72	        let mut out = canonical;
    73	        out.push('/');
    74	        out
    75	    } else {
    76	        canonical
    77	    }
    78	}
    79	
    80	#[cfg(test)]
    81	mod tests {
    82	    use super::*;
    83	    use std::path::PathBuf;
    84	
    85	    #[test]
    86	    fn empty_and_dot_produce_empty_string() {
    87	        assert_eq!(relative_path_to_posix(Path::new("")), "");
    88	        assert_eq!(relative_path_to_posix(Path::new(".")), "");
    89	    }

   101	pub async fn run_transfer(ctx: &AppContext, args: &TransferArgs, mode: TransferKind) -> Result<()> {
   102	    let src_endpoint = parse_transfer_endpoint(&args.source)?;
   103	    let raw_dst = parse_transfer_endpoint(&args.destination)?;
   104	    let pre_resolve_display = display_endpoint(&raw_dst);
   105	    let dst_endpoint = resolve_destination(&args.source, &args.destination, &src_endpoint, raw_dst);
   106	
   107	    let operation = match mode {
   108	        TransferKind::Copy => "copy",
   109	        TransferKind::Mirror => "mirror",
   110	    };
   111	    let src_display = display_endpoint(&src_endpoint);
   112	    let dst_display = display_endpoint(&dst_endpoint);
   113	
   114	    // R54-F1 (data-loss / silent bug): `--null` only works
   115	    // correctly for LOCAL COPY. Outside that envelope it's
   116	    // either destructive or silently ignored:
   117	    //   - `blit mirror --null`: the null sink discards writes,
   118	    //     but `apply_mirror_deletions` still runs (only
   119	    //     `options.dry_run` gates the actual remove_* calls)
   120	    //     and deletes destination-only files ŌĆö turning a
   121	    //     supposedly read-only benchmark into a destructive op.
   122	    //   - `blit copy --null` to/from a remote endpoint: the
   123	    //     remote push/pull paths don't implement null
   124	    //     semantics, so the flag is silently ignored and a
   125	    //     normal write happens.
   126	    //
   127	    // The narrowest safe contract for 0.1.0: --null is local
   128	    // copy only. Reject the other combinations at the CLI;
   129	    // proper plumbing of null semantics through mirror-delete
   130	    // and the remote paths is a post-release item.
   131	    if args.null {
   132	        if mode.is_mirror() {
   133	            bail!(
   134	                "--null is not supported with `blit mirror`: the \
   135	                 null sink discards writes, but mirror's \
   136	                 destination-purge step would still delete \
   137	                 destination-only files, turning what's supposed \
   138	                 to be a read-only benchmark into a destructive \
   139	                 operation. Use `blit copy --null SRC DST` (local \
   140	                 only) for read-path benchmarking."
   141	            );
   142	        }
   143	        if matches!(src_endpoint, Endpoint::Remote(_))
   144	            || matches!(dst_endpoint, Endpoint::Remote(_))
   145	        {
   146	            bail!(
   147	                "--null is not supported with remote endpoints: \
   148	                 the remote push/pull paths don't implement null \
   149	                 semantics, so the flag would be silently \
   150	                 ignored and a real write would happen. Use \
   151	                 `blit copy --null SRC DST` between two local \
   152	                 paths for read-path benchmarking."
   153	            );
   154	        }
   155	    }
   156	
   157	    // `--detach` is only honored on daemon-to-daemon
   158	    // delegated transfers. The CLI gates it up-front so a
   159	    // misuse fails before any RPCs fire ŌĆö clearer than
   160	    // letting the daemon emit a phased error mid-stream.
   161	    if args.detach {
   162	        match (&src_endpoint, &dst_endpoint) {
   163	            (Endpoint::Local(_), _) | (_, Endpoint::Local(_)) => bail!(
   164	                "--detach is only supported for remoteŌåÆremote transfers \
   165	                 (the CLI is in the byte path for any local endpoint, so \
   166	                 disconnecting would drop the bytes)"
   167	            ),
   168	            (Endpoint::Remote(_), Endpoint::Remote(_)) if args.relay_via_cli => bail!(
   169	                "--detach is incompatible with --relay-via-cli: the relay \
   170	                 path puts the CLI in the byte path, so detach would drop \
   171	                 the bytes. Drop --relay-via-cli to use the daemon-to-daemon \
   172	                 delegated path (which is the default for remoteŌåÆremote)."
   173	            ),
   174	            (Endpoint::Remote(_), Endpoint::Remote(_)) => {
   175	                // Delegated remoteŌåÆremote ŌĆö detach is valid.
   176	            }
   177	        }
   178	    }
   179	
   180	    // audit-h1 round 2: refuse `mirror --relay-via-cli` for
   181	    // remoteŌåÆremote BEFORE the destructive-confirm prompt below.
   182	    // Reviewer caught that the original h1 fix placed the gate
   183	    // inside the RemoteToRemoteRelay branch, AFTER this prompt ŌĆö
   184	    // so an operator without --yes could defeat the data-loss
   185	    // guard by answering "no" (or EOF / empty stdin) and the
   186	    // process would exit 0 with no surfacing of the unsafe
   187	    // combination. The reject-gate must precede every user-
   188	    // interaction surface for the bail's intent to land.
   189	    //
   190	    // Same data-loss reasoning as the in-route comment below.
   191	    // Symmetric with the --detach reject-gate at line 161 above
   192	    // and with the `move --relay-via-cli` gate further down.
   193	    if mode.is_mirror() && args.relay_via_cli {
   194	        if let (Endpoint::Remote(_), Endpoint::Remote(_)) = (&src_endpoint, &dst_endpoint) {
   195	            bail!(
   196	                "mirror does not support --relay-via-cli with remote \
   197	                 endpoints: the legacy relay path does not verify \
   198	                 that the source-side scan was complete, so an \
   199	                 unreadable subtree on the source daemon would let \
   200	                 mirror's destination-purge step delete destination-\
   201	                 only files that may correspond to the unreadable \
   202	                 source entries. Drop --relay-via-cli to use the \
   203	                 direct delegated path, which enforces the \
   204	                 complete-scan gate."
   205	            );
   206	        }
   207	    }
   208	
   209	    // For mirror operations, prompt unless --yes or --dry-run
   210	    if mode.is_mirror() && !args.dry_run {
   211	        let prompt = format!(
   212	            "Mirror will delete extraneous files at destination '{}'. Continue?",
   213	            dst_display
   214	        );
   215	        if !confirm_destructive_operation(&prompt, args.yes)? {
   216	            println!("Aborted.");
   217	            return Ok(());
   218	        }
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    // Banner goes to stderr so stdout stays reserved for the summary /
   222	    // JSON output. Version dropped ŌĆö `blit --version` is the right place
   223	    // for that, not every invocation.
   224	    if !args.json {
   225	        eprintln!("starting {} {} -> {}", operation, src_display, dst_display);
   226	        if args.verbose && dst_display != pre_resolve_display {
   227	            eprintln!(
   228	                "  (destination resolved by rsync trailing-slash rule: {} -> {})",
   229	                pre_resolve_display, dst_display
   230	            );
   231	        }
   232	    }
   233	
   234	    match select_transfer_route(src_endpoint, dst_endpoint, mode, args.relay_via_cli) {
   235	        TransferRoute::LocalToLocal { src, dst, mirror } => {
   236	            if !src.exists() {
   237	                bail!("source path does not exist: {}", src.display());
   238	            }
   239	            run_local_transfer(ctx, args, &src, &dst, mirror)
   240	                .await
   241	                .map(|_| ())
   242	        }
   243	        TransferRoute::LocalToRemote { src, dst, mirror } => {
   244	            if !src.exists() {
   245	                bail!("source path does not exist: {}", src.display());
   246	            }
   247	            ensure_remote_push_supported(args)?;
   248	            ensure_remote_destination_supported(&dst)?;
   249	            run_remote_push_transfer(args, Endpoint::Local(src), dst, mirror).await
   250	        }
   251	        TransferRoute::RemoteToLocal { src, dst, mirror } => {
   252	            ensure_remote_pull_supported(args)?;
   253	            ensure_remote_source_supported(&src)?;
   254	            run_remote_pull_transfer(
   255	                args, src, &dst, mirror, false, // not a move ŌĆö source survives
   256	            )
   257	            .await
   258	        }
   259	        TransferRoute::RemoteToRemoteRelay { src, dst, mirror } => {
   260	            ensure_remote_source_supported(&src)?;
   261	            ensure_remote_destination_supported(&dst)?;
   262	            // audit-h1 (data-loss): mirror is rejected up-front before
   263	            // any user-interaction surface (mirror confirm prompt) ŌĆö
   264	            // see the gate above near line 180. The relay path's
   265	            // RemoteTransferSource::scan discards unreadable_paths,
   266	            // so for mirror this risks a destination-purge run on
   267	            // an incomplete source view. Copy is fine: no purge step.
   268	            // If a future change loosens the front gate, this branch
   269	            // would silently regress, so keep a debug_assert as
   270	            // defense-in-depth.
   271	            debug_assert!(
   272	                !mirror,
   273	                "audit-h1: mirror --relay-via-cli reaching the relay branch ŌĆö \
   274	                 the front gate in run_transfer was bypassed",
   275	            );
   276	            ensure_remote_push_supported(args)?;
   277	            run_remote_push_transfer(args, Endpoint::Remote(src), dst, mirror).await
   278	        }
   279	        TransferRoute::RemoteToRemoteDelegated { src, dst, mirror } => {
   280	            ensure_remote_source_supported(&src)?;
   281	            ensure_remote_destination_supported(&dst)?;
   282	            ensure_remote_pull_supported(args)?;
   283	            run_remote_to_remote_direct(args, src, dst, mirror, false /* not a move */).await
   284	        }
   285	    }
   286	}

   289	    let src_endpoint = parse_transfer_endpoint(&args.source)?;
   290	    let raw_dst = parse_transfer_endpoint(&args.destination)?;

    60	///   [`crate::transfers::remote::run_delegated_pull`] path.
    61	/// - [`TransferRoute::RemoteToRemoteRelay`] ŌåÆ both endpoints,
    62	///   used when the user opts into `--relay-via-cli` for
    63	///   remote-to-remote ŌĆö the CLI hosts the byte path.
    64	///
    65	/// The `mirror` flag is reproduced on every variant so the
    66	/// caller doesn't need a parallel `mirror_mode` parameter; the
    67	/// route + the flag fully specify the transfer.
    68	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    69	pub enum TransferRoute {
    70	    LocalToLocal {
    71	        src: PathBuf,
    72	        dst: PathBuf,
    73	        mirror: bool,
    74	    },
    75	    LocalToRemote {
    76	        src: PathBuf,
    77	        dst: RemoteEndpoint,
    78	        mirror: bool,
    79	    },
    80	    RemoteToLocal {
    81	        src: RemoteEndpoint,
    82	        dst: PathBuf,
    83	        mirror: bool,
    84	    },
    85	    RemoteToRemoteDelegated {
    86	        src: RemoteEndpoint,
    87	        dst: RemoteEndpoint,
    88	        mirror: bool,
    89	    },
    90	    RemoteToRemoteRelay {
    91	        src: RemoteEndpoint,
    92	        dst: RemoteEndpoint,
    93	        mirror: bool,
    94	    },
    95	}
    96	
    97	/// Pure function: pick the [`TransferRoute`] for the given
    98	/// endpoint pair, verb mode, and relay choice.
    99	///
   100	/// `relay_via_cli` only affects the remoteŌåÆremote case. When
   101	/// true, the CLI host is in the byte path
   102	/// ([`TransferRoute::RemoteToRemoteRelay`]); when false, the
   103	/// daemon-to-daemon delegated pull
   104	/// ([`TransferRoute::RemoteToRemoteDelegated`]) is used.
   105	///
   106	/// No I/O, no presentation, no error cases ŌĆö the dispatch is
   107	/// total over `(Endpoint, Endpoint)`. CLI-side gates
   108	/// (`--null`, source-exists check, mirror confirmation,
   109	/// support gates) run before this function so they can produce
   110	/// CLI-shaped error messages with appropriate recovery
   111	/// guidance.
   112	pub fn select_transfer_route(
   113	    src: Endpoint,
   114	    dst: Endpoint,
   115	    kind: TransferKind,
   116	    relay_via_cli: bool,
   117	) -> TransferRoute {
   118	    let mirror = kind.is_mirror();
   119	    match (src, dst) {
   120	        (Endpoint::Local(src), Endpoint::Local(dst)) => {
   121	            TransferRoute::LocalToLocal { src, dst, mirror }
   122	        }
   123	        (Endpoint::Local(src), Endpoint::Remote(dst)) => {
   124	            TransferRoute::LocalToRemote { src, dst, mirror }
   125	        }

   199	                "blit: delegation: destination pulling from {} ({} stream(s))",
   200	                started.source_data_plane_endpoint, started.stream_count
   201	            );
   202	        }
   203	    })
   204	    .await;
   205	
   206	    drop(progress_handle);
   207	    if let Some(task) = progress_task {
   208	        let _ = task.await;
   209	    }
   210	
   211	    let state = outcome?;
   212	    if !defer_output {
   213	        print_deferred_delegated_result(args, &state);
   214	    }
   215	    Ok(state)

DEVLOG.md:16:**2026-07-07 00:45:00Z** - **CODER (otp-6b mirror on the session ŌĆö the one delete rule, claude)**: The unified session now MIRRORS (`01d9c41` + review fixes `3c99557`). The DESTINATION ŌĆö the end that holds the tree, whichever end initiated ŌĆö accumulates the COMPLETE source manifest and, at SourceDone (after every payload is written, so the tree is final), computes the extraneous set (present at dest, absent from source) and deletes it locally, filling `TransferSummary.entries_deleted`. This is the ONE delete rule that replaces the three divergent per-direction purges (local engine `apply_mirror_deletions`, daemon push `purge_extraneous_entries`, client pull `delete_listed_paths`) ŌĆö the old paths keep working until the otp-10 cutover deletes them. **blit-core** (`mirror_planner.rs`): new `plan_session_deletions(dest_root, source_files, filter)` reuses the tested `plan_from_sets`; the session manifest is files-only (dirs implicit ŌĆö `spawn_manifest_task`), so a dir's survival is derived from the parent chains of the kept files (a dir is extraneous iff no kept file lives under it), the same derivation the daemon's `plan_extraneous_entries` does. **blit-core** (`transfer_session/mod.rs`): new `mirror_delete_pass` (blocking pool) deletes files then dirs deepest-first, each containment-checked against the canonical dest root; `remove_dir` (not `remove_dir_all`) so out-of-scope content is never removed ŌĆö FilteredSubset tolerates ENOTEMPTY (dir holds filter-excluded files), All expects empty dirs. `destination_session` accumulates `source_files` when mirroring, refuses at `ManifestComplete{scan_complete=false}` (an incomplete scan would misjudge a still-unread source file extraneous ŌĆö data loss), and runs the pass at SourceDone. Scope: FilteredSubset enumerates the dest through the user filter; All enumerates the whole tree ŌĆö matching proto `MirrorMode`. `destination_open_validator` stops refusing mirror; now refuses enabled+OFF/UNSPECIFIED kind (protocol violation) and validates filter globs at OPEN. **Codex: NEEDS FIXES ŌåÆ 2 accepted + fixed** (`3c99557`). **F1 (High)**: the keep-set used `CasefoldKey`, which folded case only on Windows; the session is the first mirror path to diff a WIRE source set (source on-disk case) against the DEST filesystem, so on a case-insensitive dest (APFS/macOS) the write path treats `Foo.txt`/`foo.txt` as one file while the exact keep-set treats the dest entry as absent and DELETES the just-written file. Fixed by extending the folding `CasefoldKey` variant to macOS (`any(windows, target_os = "macos")` folds, else exact) ŌĆö case-sensitivity is a platform-default-FS property, which is what the key models; this also improves the retired paths on macOS. **F2 (Med)**: `mirror_delete_pass` skipped `win_fs::clear_readonly_recursive`, so a read-only extraneous entry would fail the pass on Windows (the two old executors clear it first) ŌĆö fixed under `cfg(windows)`. Verdict `.review/results/otp-6b.gpt-verdict.md` (raw `.codex.md`). **Guard proofs (run live on Linux)**: (1) neutralize the delete pass (`if false`) ŌåÆ `mirror_all_purges_extraneous_under_both_initiators` FAILS (stale file remains); (2) neutralize the scan-complete guard ŌåÆ `mirror_refused_when_source_scan_incomplete` no longer refuses. Both fixes are macOS/Windows-specific and CANNOT be guard-proven on the Linux dev box: a cfg-gated `CasefoldKey` fold test runs on macOS/Windows CI, a Linux exact-match test pins no-regression, and the F2 `win_fs` call matches the two existing executors verbatim (windows-latest CI verifies). Removed the obsolete `mirror_request_is_refused_until_its_slice_lands`. 5 new mirror tests (all-purge under both initiators, filtered-subset preserve, all-purge-out-of-scope, enabled-without-scope refused, scan-incomplete refused). Suite 1524 ŌåÆ **1529/0** (+5 mirror ŌłÆ1 obsolete +1 Linux casefold). fmt/clippy clean. **otp-6 fully closed** (6a filters + 6b mirror). Next: **otp-7** (resume block phase ŌĆö ordering + stale-partial pins per the plan's RELIABLE exception). Known gaps: Unicode (non-ASCII) case folding still approximate; case-insensitive Linux mounts / case-sensitive macOS volumes are undetectable by a compile-time cfg (documented, rsync/robocopy share this). (Unrelated `Cargo.lock` drift still unstaged.)
DEVLOG.md:20:**2026-07-06 20:15:00Z** - **CODER (otp-5b-2 pull data-plane resize, claude)**: The pull data plane now grows mid-transfer via the sf-2 shape correction, lifting otp-5b-1's single-stream cap (`d579365` + review fix `773a877`). The resize control-lane frames (`DataPlaneResize{ADD}`/`DataPlaneResizeAck`) are IDENTICAL to push; only socket **acquisition** flips per connection role ŌĆö the SOURCE **responder** ACCEPTS each epoch-N socket off its bound listener, the DESTINATION **initiator** DIALS it. All resize machinery is reused. **blit-core** (`data_plane.rs`): `SourceDataPlane` gained a `SourceSockets` enum (`Dial{host,tcp_port}`=initiator/push, `Accept{listener}`=responder/pull) replacing the `host`/`tcp_port`/`resizable` fields; `accept_source_data_plane` retains its bound listener instead of dropping it; `propose_resize` lost the `!resizable` early-return (both directions propose); `add_stream` branches ŌĆö the initiator dials the epoch-N socket (unchanged), the responder `accept_authenticated`s the socket the DEST dials after its ack (`session_token ŌĆ¢ sub_token`), then hands it to the elastic pipeline via `SinkControl::Add`. The accept is bounded + unambiguous (Ōēż1 resize in flight via the dial's `pending_epoch`; epoch-0 already accepted ŌćÆ next connection is exactly this resize ŌĆö no arm set needed on the SOURCE). `InitiatorReceivePlaneRun` retained host/port/token/sink and gained `add_dialed_stream` (dial epoch-N, spawn receive worker, bump settled count). **blit-core** (`mod.rs`): `destination_session`'s initiator branch seeds `resize_live` from the epoch-0 streams and `resize_ceiling` from the capacity THIS end advertised (not a fresh local read ŌĆö see F1), replacing the otp-5b-1 `(0,0)` that made every `Resize` a violation; the `Frame::Resize` handler branches arm (responder) vs dial (initiator). Ordering: the DEST initiator dials BEFORE it acks, so the SOURCE responder ŌĆö which accepts on the ack ŌĆö never commits to an accept the peer did not dial; a dial failure is fatal (symmetric with push's SOURCE dial), firing before any commit. **Codex: NEEDS FIXES ŌåÆ 1 Low accepted + fixed.** F1 (Low, `773a877`): the DEST initiator's resize ceiling read a fresh `local_receiver_capacity()` instead of the `receiver_capacity` it advertised in `SessionOpen` (`run_destination` keeps a caller-provided profile); the SOURCE responder's dial clamps to the advertised value, so the two ends could disagree on the ceiling. Now reads `negotiated.open.receiver_capacity.max_streams` ŌĆö both ends use the identical bound. Same-build happy path was already protected (the SOURCE never proposes beyond what it clamped to), hence Low; the fix aligns the code with its own comment. Verdict `.review/results/otp-5b-2-pull-data-plane-resize.gpt-verdict.md` (raw `.codex.md`). Guard proof (run live, on the fixed code): force the DEST initiator ceiling to 0 ŌåÆ `pull_data_plane_shape_corrects_to_more_than_one_stream` FAILS "settled at 1" while `pull_data_plane_single_stream_lands_bytes` still passes (byte correctness independent of stream count); restored ŌåÆ both pass. Tests 1521 ŌåÆ **1522** (+1 roles `pull_data_plane_shape_corrects_to_more_than_one_stream`: 10k tiny files, DEST-initiator/SOURCE-responder over real loopback TCP, `data_plane_streams > 1`; the single-stream test's rationale comment corrected ŌĆö small tree below the shape threshold, not a disabled resize). fmt/clippy clean. Next: **otp-6** (mirror + filters on the session, one delete rule) ŌĆö otp-5b-3 (mid-transfer cancel over the pull data plane) is optional (the CANCELLED framing is already role-agnostic; a distinct guard may be unnecessary). (Unrelated `Cargo.lock` drift still unstaged ŌĆö STATE open item.)
DEVLOG.md:26:**2026-07-06 05:37:00Z** - **CODER (otp-4b-3 deterministic mid-transfer cancel e2e, claude)**: A `CancelJob` fired while payload bytes are in flight over the session's TCP data plane now surfaces to the client as `SessionFault{CANCELLED}` ŌĆö the peer's framed abort reason ŌĆö instead of the data-plane `Broken pipe` (INTERNAL) the cancel also causes, and never hangs (`3ae0a5f` + review fixes `a530005`, `46cc4bb`; records `db9b63d`). **Problem found while building the e2e** (throwaway gated-source experiment): the daemon side was already correct (otp-4a codex F1 ŌĆö the served `Transfer` dispatcher drops `run_destination` and frames `SessionError{CANCELLED}`), but the SOURCE only consulted the control lane when parked at `events.recv()`. During the payload **drain** (`SourceDataPlane::finish`, where a push spends its byte-transfer wall time) it awaited only the data-plane pipeline, so a cancel dropped the destination ŌåÆ the source's socket write hit `Broken pipe` first ŌåÆ the client surfaced INTERNAL, and a worker blocked reading a slow file (never writing) ŌåÆ the socket break never unblocked it ŌåÆ **client hung**. **Fix** (`transfer_session/mod.rs`): `source_send_half` races the drain against a peer-framed fault on the control lane. `recv_peer_fault` (strict; a `biased` `select!` arm against `dp.finish()`) wins if the fault arrives while the drain is still pending ŌĆö dropping the unfinished `finish()` future drops the `SourceDataPlane`, whose `AbortOnDrop` stops in-flight workers (this is what makes the blocked-reader case terminate as CANCELLED instead of hanging). `prefer_peer_fault` (lenient) handles the socket-break-first ordering at BOTH the `queue()` and `finish()` error paths ŌĆö prefers the framed reason within `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT`, skipping still-in-flight `Need`/`ResizeAck` events (a `Need` can queue ahead of `CANCELLED` during the payload loop), else the raw data-plane error. **Codex: 3 passes.** Pass 1 (`3ae0a5f`) NEEDS FIXES, 3/3 accepted: F1 (High) `dp.queue()` not fault-preferred (multi-file backpressure cancel ŌåÆ DATA_PLANE_FAILED); F2 (Med) the e2e's bytes-flowed gate fired on a 256 KiB local duplex before TCP; F3 (Med) `recv_peer_fault` silently dropped non-fault drain events. Pass 2 (`a530005`) NEEDS FIXES, 1/1 accepted: the F1+F3 pair interacted ŌĆö routing `queue()` errors through the now-strict `recv_peer_fault` could surface a spurious `PROTOCOL_VIOLATION` from a legitimately-queued `Need`; fixed by splitting the helpers (strict `recv_peer_fault` for the live drain select arm only; lenient `prefer_peer_fault` for both error paths). Pass 3 (`46cc4bb`) **PASS**. Guard proofs: e2e `mid_transfer_cancel_surfaces_cancelled_over_the_data_plane` (revert the select ŌåÆ client hangs ŌåÆ 10 s timeout FAIL), unit `prefer_peer_fault_prefers_a_framed_fault` (revert ŌåÆ wrong code) + `prefer_peer_fault_skips_inflight_needs_to_reach_the_fault` (pass-2 regression guard). Suite 1513 ŌåÆ **1516/0**, fmt/clippy clean. Verdict `.review/results/otp-4b3-data-plane.gpt-verdict.md`. Known gap: a cancel while a worker is blocked reading a slow local file *inside* an early `queue()` (channel full) can still hang until the peer's stall guard fires ŌĆö pre-existing slow-local-read pathology, not cancel-specific. **otp-4b fully closed** (4b-1/4b-2/4b-3). DEVLOG.md:28:**2026-07-06 00:30:00Z** - **CODER (otp-4b-2 resize + multi-stream + sf-2 pin, claude)**: The unified session's data plane now grows mid-transfer ŌĆö the zero-knowledge single-stream grant shape-corrects upward as the need list accumulates, over real sockets (`dce56de`). **SOURCE owns the live dial** (`TransferDial::conservative_within(receiver_capacity)`, seeded to the granted epoch-0 count; pool provisioned for `ceiling_max_streams`, matching old push's lazy-alloc rationale). As needs accumulate it re-runs the shape table (`initial_stream_proposal(needed_bytes, needed_count, ceiling)`) and calls `propose_shape_resize` ŌĆö one ADD per epoch, one in flight (the dial's `pending_epoch` CAS); mints a 16-byte sub-token, sends `DataPlaneResize{ADD}` on the control lane, and on `DataPlaneResizeAck` dials the epoch-N socket (`session_token ŌĆ¢ sub_token`) and `SinkControl::Add`s it to the now-**elastic** pipeline (`execute_sink_pipeline_elastic`). `source_send_half` gained `needed_bytes/count` accumulators, `maybe_propose_resize`, `process_source_event` (ResizeAck ŌåÆ dial + settle + propose-next ramp), and `resolve_in_flight_resize` (drains the one in-flight proposal BEFORE `dp.finish()` so no armed dest slot orphans). **DESTINATION** runs a resize-aware `accept_loop` (`ResponderDataPlane::spawn` ŌåÆ select over arm-channel / bounded accept / worker-join); the control loop handles `Frame::Resize` (ceiling-checked arm + `resize_live` bump + `DataPlaneResizeAck`), and at SourceDone `finish()`es the run for the settled stream count on `DestinationOutcome.data_plane_streams`. **Orphan-free by construction**: a source resize-dial failure is FATAL (session faults ŌåÆ AbortOnDrop kills the dest accept loop), a deliberate simplification vs old push's arm-TTL recovery (noted in the finding doc). **Bug caught in pre-commit e2e**: the dest accept loop busy-spun once `arm_tx` dropped ŌĆö a closed `mpsc` resolves `recv()` to `None` every poll and, as the biased-first select arm, starved `join_next`, so finished receive workers were never collected and `finish()` hung (reproduced on the gRPC data-plane e2e); fixed by parking the arm branch on `pending()` once closed (the same guard `execute_sink_pipeline_elastic` uses). sf-2 pin ported: `many_tiny_files_shape_correct_to_more_than_one_stream` (10k tiny files over the data plane settle `data_plane_streams > 1`, guard-proven: neuter the proposal ŌåÆ settles at 1 ŌåÆ pin fails). **Codex: PASS, no findings** (source resize sequencing, dest accept/finish teardown, byte accounting, StallGuard wiring, sf-2 pin all sound; verdict `.review/results/otp-4b2-data-plane.gpt-verdict.md`). Comment-truth: `RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE`'s false "matches the send side" claim rewritten (receive is deliberately 1 MiB vs the sender's 16ŌĆō64 MiB; the asymmetry is legal ŌĆö no per-chunk framing); BufferPool header example now shows the constructor. The review assessment surfaced four facts the finding doc didn't know, recorded here as input to the slice-2 re-scope: **(1)** the 1 MiB frame cap is load-bearing correctness, not just cadence ŌĆö tonic 0.14's default 4 MiB decode limit (`DEFAULT_MAX_RECV_MESSAGE_SIZE`, no `max_decoding_message_size` override anywhere in the workspace) means pre-slice-1 gRPC-fallback transfers of files >4 MiB should fail at decode, since `tuning.rs` emits 16/32/64 MiB chunks and `pull_sync.rs:515` passed `tuning.chunk_bytes` straight into `GrpcServerStreamingSink`. Version-skew residual: a new client against an old daemon still receives uncapped frames. **(2)** The bigger H3 hole is missing client-side HTTP/2 keepalive: daemon pings clients (`main.rs:138`) but all three client channel builders (`pull.rs:239`, `push/client/mod.rs:307`, `blit-app/src/client.rs:38` ŌĆö already-drifted near-duplicates) set only `connect_timeout`, so a dead daemon hangs `message().await` forever; ~3 lines of `Endpoint` keepalive config cover dead-peer/black-hole at transport level and shrink slice 2's watchdog scope to wedged-but-alive peers only. **(3)** Fallback throughput is governed by HTTP/2 flow-control windows, not frame size ŌĆö hyper defaults: client 2 MiB stream / 5 MiB conn; daemon server 1 MiB conn total ŌåÆ hardware-independent push-fallback ceiling on high-BDP links; `http2_adaptive_window(true)` is the no-tuning fix. **(4)** `clamp_fallback_chunk_size(x.max(1MiB))` ŌēĪ const 1 MiB ŌĆö the sinks' `chunk_bytes` param is now inert and misleading; root cause is a TCP transport parameter (`chunk_bytes`) embedded in the transport-agnostic `PlannedPayloads` (planner payload composition itself is sound). Owner direction: slice 2 re-scope deferred until after a repo-wide design-coherence review (plan doc next). Sentinel cleared, `REVIEW.md` updated to verified (`[x]`).

Four findings: **#1 Medium (active-gauge race).** `format_completion_line` was reading `active_transfers` while the just-finished RPC's `_guard` was still in scope, so a single completed transfer logged `active=1` ŌĆö misleading for an end-of-RPC summary. Now `active=N` reflects state AFTER the just-finished RPC is removed from the gauge. **#2 Medium (missing RPC coverage).** `delegated_pull` increments `pull_ops` + the active gauge inside `run_delegated_pull` (`delegated_pull.rs:227`) but never emitted its own completion line ŌĆö the field would only become visible on a later push/pull log. Same for `purge`. DEVLOG.md:194:**2026-05-02 19:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed F2 from `docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md` ŌĆö the highest-severity remaining baseline finding. The lexical `safe_join` chokepoint catches `../`/abs/UNC/Windows-shaped wire paths but doesn't follow symlinks, so a pre-existing symlink inside a module pointing outside the root (e.g. `module/escape -> /etc`) would have any daemon read/write follow it. New `path_safety::contained_join` (and `verify_contained` for already-resolved targets) walks to the deepest existing ancestor, canonicalizes, and confirms `starts_with(canonical_module_root)`. 10 unit tests cover symlink-escape rejection (top-level, deep, parent-of-nonexistent), legit intra-module symlinks, lexical-traversal rejection, and the empty-rel single-file case. Wired into every daemon site that touches a path under a module root: `service/core.rs` (list, find, du, purge), `service/admin.rs` (delete_rel_paths_sync, stream_disk_usage, stream_find_entries), `service/pull.rs` and `service/pull_sync.rs` (pull entry-point), `service/push/data_plane.rs` (file dest + tar shard apply), `service/push/control.rs` (file_requires_upload). Added a separate `canonical_root: PathBuf` field on `ModuleConfig` because the push handler mutates `module.path` to bake in destination subpaths (rsync "copy into here" semantics) ŌĆö containment must check against the never-mutated original. New integration tests in `crates/blit-cli/tests/f2_chroot_containment.rs` spin up a real daemon, place a symlink inside the module pointing outside, attempt to pull through it, assert the daemon refuses with a containment error, and verify the sensitive sibling file was not copied. Companion test confirms legit intra-module symlinks (`latest -> v1`) still work. **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (186 lib + 20 daemon + integration suites, all green). F2 closes the last release-blocking security finding from the original baseline review.
DEVLOG.md:200:**2026-05-02 16:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 9 finding R9-F1 (Low). The R8-F2 fix (rejecting stream EOF without UploadComplete) was previously verified by code review only ŌĆö the new framing-helper unit tests covered R8-F1 size/cap rules but not the actual EOF path through `receive_fallback_data`.
