DEVLOG.md:202:**2026-05-02 15:45:00Z** - **ACTION**: Closed Round 8 review findings R8-F1 and R8-F2 from `docs/reviews/followup_review_2026-05-02.md`. Both bugs were in the daemon's gRPC push fallback receive loop (`receive_fallback_data` in `crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs`) ŌĆö the framing layer that runs *before* the shared `tar_safety` helper sees the buffer. **R8-F1** (Medium ŌĆö DoS): the chunk accumulator was capped only by an 8 MiB initial reservation; the actual `Vec` grew unbounded. `archive_size == 0` skipped the overflow check entirely, and `archive_size > MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` was bypassed at the framing layer. Reject zero archive_size when files are present, reject `archive_size > MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` at TarShardHeader, and enforce both the declared size and the local cap on every chunk via a new `check_fallback_chunk_overflow` helper. **R8-F2** (Medium ŌĆö silent partial success): stream EOF was treated as graceful end. But FileManifest and TarShardHeader remove entries from `pending` before bytes arrive, so a client could send a header, close the stream, and the final `pending.is_empty()` check would pass despite no data ever landing. Track `upload_complete_seen` and bail on EOF without UploadComplete or with `active.is_some()`. Extracted `validate_fallback_shard_archive_size` and `check_fallback_chunk_overflow` as private helpers so the rules are unit-testable without spinning up a full gRPC server. 7 new framing tests pin every boundary condition (zero size, at-cap, above cap, declared overflow, local-cap overflow, u64 overflow, within-bounds). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` (166 lib + 17 daemon + integration suites, all green).
DEVLOG.md:270:**2025-01-28 12:00:00Z** - **ACTION**: Implemented resumable file copy with block-level comparison. Added `resume_copy_file` function in `blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs` that compares source and destination block-by-block (default 1 MiB blocks), skips matching blocks, overwrites mismatches, appends remaining bytes, and truncates if dest is longer. This enables resuming interrupted transfers and efficiently updating files with localized changes. 5 unit tests covering: new file, partial resume, identical file (all blocks skipped), truncation, and corrupted block repair. Integration with CLI `--resume` flag pending. **Tests**: `cargo test -p blit-core resume` (5 passed).

Both findings flag a needed owner design call (skip/report/sanitize/fail-fast policy) before any code ŌĆö filed, not fixed. Next: otp-7 (unrelated; continues per `docs/plan/OTP7_RESUME.md`).

DEVLOG.md:154:**2026-05-05 19:30:00Z** - **FIX**: Round 44 review of commit `da6ced2`. **R44-F1 (Medium)**: predictor train/query feature mismatch. The pre-pipeline query in `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs` used `(all_headers.len(), total_bytes)` (scan-side workload), but `record_performance_history` recorded `summary.copied_files` for `PerformanceRecord.file_count`. On any incremental run the predictor saw "predict 1000 files" then trained on "5 files actually copied" ŌĆö estimates drifted badly. Fix: added `scanned_files: usize` and `scanned_bytes: u64` to `LocalMirrorSummary` (`crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/summary.rs`) with a load-bearing rustdoc explaining the scan-vs-copy split; populated at every summary construction site (streaming pipeline, NoWork, Tiny, Huge, JournalSkip, single-file copy); `record_performance_history` now reads `summary.scanned_{files,bytes}` for the record's feature fields. The bucket-shape counters (`tar_shard_*`, `raw_bundle_*`, `large_*`) still reflect actual writes ŌĆö they feed `derive_local_plan_tuning` which heuristically sizes destination buckets from past apply behavior, not scan size. Extracted `build_performance_record` from `record_performance_history` so the contract is unit-testable without polluting the global JSONL. Two new tests in `orchestrator::history::tests`: `record_uses_scanned_features_not_copied` (would have failed pre-fix on a 1000-scanned/5-copied incremental) and `bucket_counts_still_reflect_actual_writes` (regression guard against accidentally rerouting bucket counters through scan stats). **R44-F2 (Low)**: `blit profile --json` shape was unasserted. The pre-fix commit message claimed top-level `"predictor": null` for the empty-state, but actual output emits `{"copy": null, "mirror": null}` (predictor file loads even when no profile yet has training data). Picked the structured shape ŌĆö strictly more informative ŌĆö and pinned it in `test_utils_profile_json` (`crates/blit-cli/tests/blit_utils.rs`) with assertions covering both empty and trained states. **R44 plan note**: ┬¦2.8 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` is correctly framed now as "predictor observability and training," not "adaptive planning behavior" ŌĆö the predictor is queried, surfaced via `--verbose` and `blit profile --json`, and audit-able, but the Tiny fast-path still does not consult it for routing. Added a Status block to the plan section documenting this. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 406 pass / 0 fail (was 404, +2 history regression tests).
DEVLOG.md:156:**2026-05-05 18:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: ┬¦2.8 phase 2 of `docs/plan/RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` ŌĆö orchestrator and `blit profile` now actually query the predictor. Three load-bearing changes: (1) `crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs` introduces a `plan_done = Instant::now()` checkpoint between the planner stage and the pipeline so `planner_duration_ms` and `transfer_duration_ms` are correctly attributed; pre-fix both fields fed `record_performance_history` got the same whole-run time, so v1 predictor training collapsed into a single regressor. (2) Just before kicking off `execute_sink_pipeline`, the orchestrator queries `predictor.predict(DurationKind::Total/Planner/Transfer, ...)` with the just-scanned `all_headers.len()` and `total_bytes`; populates `LocalMirrorSummary.predictor_estimate` (new field of type `PredictorEstimate { planner_ms, transfer_ms, total_ms, observations, fallback_depth }` in `summary.rs`). `--verbose` now emits two lines: a "Predictor estimate: ..." pre-run line and a "Predictor delta: ..." post-run line showing predicted-vs-actual percent error per phase. (3) `crates/blit-cli/src/profile.rs::run_profile` now calls `predictor.coefficients_for(mode-only, ...)` for both Copy and Mirror, surfaces the result as a coefficients block in human output (`alpha_ms_per_file`, `beta_ms_per_mb`, `gamma_ms` per planner/transfer pair) and as a `predictor.{copy,mirror}` JSON object under `--json`. Smoke test: `blit profile --json` returns the new `predictor` key (null when no v2 profile yet); `blit copy` --verbose under streaming-planner workloads will emit the new predictor lines once 5+ observations accumulate. Tiny fast-path extension (the planner-overhead-dominance signal in the plan) deferred to post-0.1.0 ŌĆö extending the fast_path scan budget risks edge cases on memory-bounded large-tree workloads, and the predictor's now-load-bearing model is only freshly trained on v2 data; revisit once we have multi-week observability under the new schema. **Tests**: `cargo test --workspace` 404 pass / 0 fail.
DEVLOG.md:204:**2026-05-02 14:30:00Z** - **ACTION**: Round 7 cleanup ŌĆö extracted shared `tar_safety` primitive in `blit-core/src/remote/transfer/tar_safety.rs` and migrated all three tar-shard receive sites onto it: `pull.rs::apply_pull_tar_shard` (gRPC fallback), `sink.rs::write_tar_shard_payload` (TCP data plane + local-local), `blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs::apply_tar_shard_sync` (daemon push receive). The migration closed a previously-latent High-severity bug on the daemon side: `apply_tar_shard_sync` was calling `Entry::unpack`, so an authenticated push client could ship a tar shard with a Symlink entry at a benign path pointing at `/etc/passwd` and a later push to that path would write through the symlink ŌĆö same R5-F2 class as the pull side, but server-side. New regression test `apply_tar_shard_rejects_symlink_entry` proves the daemon now rejects non-regular entries up front. The shared helper also brought R6-F1 size bounds and R6-F3 mtime/permissions preservation to `sink.rs` and the daemon, where they were missing. 8 new unit tests in `tar_safety::tests`; net +8 lib tests workspace-wide (166 total). **Tests**: `cargo fmt`; `cargo test --workspace` all green.
DEVLOG.md:232:**2026-04-24 03:15:00Z** - **FIX**: Fixed single-file remote push crash ŌĆö `blit copy FILE server:/mod/` previously died with "opening FILE/ during payload planning: Not a directory". Root cause was two-sided: on the client, `filter_readable_headers` and `build_tar_shard` computed `source_root.join(&rel)` where `rel=""` for single-file sources, which on Unix preserves a trailing `/` and makes `File::open` reject with ENOTDIR. On the daemon, `resolve_relative_path` folded empty paths to `"."` (which broke `module.path.join("")` = wanted single file, but got `module.path/.`), and the subsequent `module.path.join(empty_rel)` added another trailing `/`. Fix applies the `rel.is_empty() ŌåÆ use root directly` pattern in three places on the client side (matching `FsTransferSource::open_file`'s existing handling), and adds two new helpers on the daemon side: `resolve_manifest_relative_path` preserves empty as empty for per-file manifest entries, and `resolve_dest_path(base, rel)` handles the empty-rel join case. Swapped all four push-side `resolve_relative_path` callers and three `module.path.join` sites. Regression tests in `crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_push_single_file.rs` pin both the container-dir (`blit copy FILE server:/mod/`) and rename (`blit copy FILE server:/mod/new.txt`) cases. Annotated all four `docs/bugs/*.md` files with their resolution status. **Tests**: 173 passed (+2 remote push single-file), clippy clean.

    16	**2026-07-07 00:45:00Z** - **CODER (otp-6b mirror on the session ŌĆö the one delete rule, claude)**: The unified session now MIRRORS (`01d9c41` + review fixes `3c99557`). The DESTINATION ŌĆö the end that holds the tree, whichever end initiated ŌĆö accumulates the COMPLETE source manifest and, at SourceDone (after every payload is written, so the tree is final), computes the extraneous set (present at dest, absent from source) and deletes it locally, filling `TransferSummary.entries_deleted`. This is the ONE delete rule that replaces the three divergent per-direction purges (local engine `apply_mirror_deletions`, daemon push `purge_extraneous_entries`, client pull `delete_listed_paths`) ŌĆö the old paths keep working until the otp-10 cutover deletes them. **blit-core** (`mirror_planner.rs`): new `plan_session_deletions(dest_root, source_files, filter)` reuses the tested `plan_from_sets`; the session manifest is files-only (dirs implicit ŌĆö `spawn_manifest_task`), so a dir's survival is derived from the parent chains of the kept files (a dir is extraneous iff no kept file lives under it), the same derivation the daemon's `plan_extraneous_entries` does. **blit-core** (`transfer_session/mod.rs`): new `mirror_delete_pass` (blocking pool) deletes files then dirs deepest-first, each containment-checked against the canonical dest root; `remove_dir` (not `remove_dir_all`) so out-of-scope content is never removed ŌĆö FilteredSubset tolerates ENOTEMPTY (dir holds filter-excluded files), All expects empty dirs. `destination_session` accumulates `source_files` when mirroring, refuses at `ManifestComplete{scan_complete=false}` (an incomplete scan would misjudge a still-unread source file extraneous ŌĆö data loss), and runs the pass at SourceDone. Scope: FilteredSubset enumerates the dest through the user filter; All enumerates the whole tree ŌĆö matching proto `MirrorMode`. `destination_open_validator` stops refusing mirror; now refuses enabled+OFF/UNSPECIFIED kind (protocol violation) and validates filter globs at OPEN. **Codex: NEEDS FIXES ŌåÆ 2 accepted + fixed** (`3c99557`). **F1 (High)**: the keep-set used `CasefoldKey`, which folded case only on Windows; the session is the first mirror path to diff a WIRE source set (source on-disk case) against the DEST filesystem, so on a case-insensitive dest (APFS/macOS) the write path treats `Foo.txt`/`foo.txt` as one file while the exact keep-set treats the dest entry as absent and DELETES the just-written file. Fixed by extending the folding `CasefoldKey` variant to macOS (`any(windows, target_os = "macos")` folds, else exact) ŌĆö case-sensitivity is a platform-default-FS property, which is what the key models; this also improves the retired paths on macOS. **F2 (Med)**: `mirror_delete_pass` skipped `win_fs::clear_readonly_recursive`, so a read-only extraneous entry would fail the pass on Windows (the two old executors clear it first) ŌĆö fixed under `cfg(windows)`. Verdict `.review/results/otp-6b.gpt-verdict.md` (raw `.codex.md`). **Guard proofs (run live on Linux)**: (1) neutralize the delete pass (`if false`) ŌåÆ `mirror_all_purges_extraneous_under_both_initiators` FAILS (stale file remains); (2) neutralize the scan-complete guard ŌåÆ `mirror_refused_when_source_scan_incomplete` no longer refuses. Both fixes are macOS/Windows-specific and CANNOT be guard-proven on the Linux dev box: a cfg-gated `CasefoldKey` fold test runs on macOS/Windows CI, a Linux exact-match test pins no-regression, and the F2 `win_fs` call matches the two existing executors verbatim (windows-latest CI verifies). Removed the obsolete `mirror_request_is_refused_until_its_slice_lands`. 5 new mirror tests (all-purge under both initiators, filtered-subset preserve, all-purge-out-of-scope, enabled-without-scope refused, scan-incomplete refused).     20	**2026-07-06 20:15:00Z** - **CODER (otp-5b-2 pull data-plane resize, claude)**: The pull data plane now grows mid-transfer via the sf-2 shape correction, lifting otp-5b-1's single-stream cap (`d579365` + review fix `773a877`). The resize control-lane frames (`DataPlaneResize{ADD}`/`DataPlaneResizeAck`) are IDENTICAL to push; only socket **acquisition** flips per connection role ŌĆö the SOURCE **responder** ACCEPTS each epoch-N socket off its bound listener, the DESTINATION **initiator** DIALS it. All resize machinery is reused. **blit-core** (`data_plane.rs`): `SourceDataPlane` gained a `SourceSockets` enum (`Dial{host,tcp_port}`=initiator/push, `Accept{listener}`=responder/pull) replacing the `host`/`tcp_port`/`resizable` fields; `accept_source_data_plane` retains its bound listener instead of dropping it; `propose_resize` lost the `!resizable` early-return (both directions propose); `add_stream` branches ŌĆö the initiator dials the epoch-N socket (unchanged), the responder `accept_authenticated`s the socket the DEST dials after its ack (`session_token ŌĆ¢ sub_token`), then hands it to the elastic pipeline via `SinkControl::Add`. The accept is bounded + unambiguous (Ōēż1 resize in flight via the dial's `pending_epoch`; epoch-0 already accepted ŌćÆ next connection is exactly this resize ŌĆö no arm set needed on the SOURCE). `InitiatorReceivePlaneRun` retained host/port/token/sink and gained `add_dialed_stream` (dial epoch-N, spawn receive worker, bump settled count). **blit-core** (`mod.rs`): `destination_session`'s initiator branch seeds `resize_live` from the epoch-0 streams and `resize_ceiling` from the capacity THIS end advertised (not a fresh local read ŌĆö see F1), replacing the otp-5b-1 `(0,0)` that made every `Resize` a violation; the `Frame::Resize` handler branches arm (responder) vs dial (initiator). Ordering: the DEST initiator dials BEFORE it acks, so the SOURCE responder ŌĆö which accepts on the ack ŌĆö never commits to an accept the peer did not dial; a dial failure is fatal (symmetric with push's SOURCE dial), firing before any commit. **Codex: NEEDS FIXES ŌåÆ 1 Low accepted + fixed.** F1 (Low, `773a877`): the DEST initiator's resize ceiling read a fresh `local_receiver_capacity()` instead of the `receiver_capacity` it advertised in `SessionOpen` (`run_destination` keeps a caller-provided profile); the SOURCE responder's dial clamps to the advertised value, so the two ends could disagree on the ceiling. Now reads `negotiated.open.receiver_capacity.max_streams` ŌĆö both ends use the identical bound. Same-build happy path was already protected (the SOURCE never proposes beyond what it clamped to), hence Low; the fix aligns the code with its own comment. Verdict `.review/results/otp-5b-2-pull-data-plane-resize.gpt-verdict.md` (raw `.codex.md`).     60	        skip_unchanged: options.skip_unchanged,
    61	        checksum: options.checksum,
    62	        compare_mode: snapshot_compare_mode(options),
    63	        workers: options.workers,
    64	    };
    65	
    66	    let mode = if options.mirror {
    67	        TransferMode::Mirror
    68	    } else {
    69	        TransferMode::Copy
    70	    };
    71	
    72	    // R44-F1: train against scanned features so the predictor's
    73	    // training inputs match its query inputs. The orchestrator
    74	    // queries `predict(...)` with `all_headers.len()` (scanned
    75	    // count) and `total_bytes` (scanned bytes); pre-fix the record
    76	    // was populated with `summary.copied_files`, so the predictor
    77	    // saw a different feature vector at training time than at
    78	    // query time, and predictions drifted on every incremental
    79	    // workload. The `total_bytes` field on the record was already
    80	    // scanned-bytes by accident; this aligns both axes deliberately.
    81	    //
    82	    // `summary.copied_files` and the per-bucket counts
    83	    // (tar_shard_files / raw_bundle_files / large_tasks) still
    84	    // reflect actual writes ŌĆö they're the load-bearing inputs for
    85	    // `derive_local_plan_tuning`'s bucket-target heuristics, which
    86	    // are computed from observed apply behavior, not scan size.
    87	    let mut record = PerformanceRecord::new(
    88	        mode,
    89	        None,
    90	        None,
    91	        summary.scanned_files,
    92	        summary.scanned_bytes,
    93	        options_snapshot,
    94	        fast_path.map(|s| s.to_string()),
    95	        planner_duration_ms,
    96	        transfer_duration_ms,
    97	        0,
    98	        0,
    99	    );
   100	    record.tar_shard_tasks = summary.tar_shard_tasks as u32;
   101	    record.tar_shard_files = summary.tar_shard_files as u32;
   102	    record.tar_shard_bytes = summary.tar_shard_bytes;
   103	    record.raw_bundle_tasks = summary.raw_bundle_tasks as u32;
   104	    record.raw_bundle_files = summary.raw_bundle_files as u32;
   105	    record.raw_bundle_bytes = summary.raw_bundle_bytes;
   106	    record.large_tasks = summary.large_tasks as u32;
   107	    record.large_bytes = summary.large_bytes;
   108	
   109	    record
   110	}

   176	impl PerformanceRecord {
   177	    #[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
   178	    pub fn new(
   179	        mode: TransferMode,
   180	        source_fs: Option<String>,
   181	        dest_fs: Option<String>,
   182	        file_count: usize,
   183	        total_bytes: u64,
   184	        options: OptionSnapshot,
   185	        fast_path: Option<String>,
   186	        planner_duration_ms: u128,
   187	        transfer_duration_ms: u128,
   188	        stall_events: u32,
   189	        error_count: u32,
   190	    ) -> Self {
   191	        // R56-F1: derive `run_kind` from the call-site inputs. The
   192	        // callers that need a specific kind (bench verbs, future
   193	        // synthetic source) should mutate `record.run_kind` after
   194	        // construction; this default infers from existing fields so
   195	        // we don't have to thread a new parameter through every
   196	        // caller right now.
   197	        let run_kind = if options.dry_run {
   198	            RunKind::DryRun
   199	        } else if fast_path.as_deref() == Some("null_sink") {
   200	            RunKind::NullSink
   201	        } else {
   202	            RunKind::Real
   203	        };
   204	        let now = SystemTime::now()
   205	            .duration_since(UNIX_EPOCH)
   206	            .unwrap_or_default();
   207	        Self {
   208	            schema_version: CURRENT_SCHEMA_VERSION,
   209	            timestamp_epoch_ms: now.as_millis(),
   210	            mode,
   211	            run_kind,
   212	            source_fs,
   213	            dest_fs,
   214	            file_count,
   215	            total_bytes,
   216	            options,
   217	            fast_path,
   218	            planner_duration_ms,

     1	# DECISIONS ŌĆö settled choices
     2	
     3	**Status**: Active
     4	
     5	Append-only ledger of decisions that future sessions must not relitigate or miss.
     6	Add entries via the `decision` procedure in `docs/agent/PROTOCOL.md`. Newest last.
     7	When a decision supersedes plan text, the plan text gets edited in the same
     8	session ŌĆö this file is the index, not a substitute for fixing the doc.
     9	
    10	Format:
    11	
    12	```
    13	## D-<YYYY-MM-DD>-<n> ŌĆö <short title>
    14	- Decision: <one line>
    15	- Why: <one line>
    16	- Supersedes: <doc ┬¦/decision ID, or "nothing">
    17	```
    18

    20	
    21	## D-2026-05-31-1 ŌĆö v0.1.0 shipped; release plan frozen
    22	- Decision: `RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md` is a frozen reference, no longer the active source of truth.
    23	- Why: 0.1.0 tagged 2026-05-31; the plan served its purpose.
    24	- Supersedes: RELEASE_PLAN_v2_2026-05-04.md as active plan.
    25	
    26	## D-2026-05-31-2 ŌĆö Pick-not-Type TUI direction
    27	- Decision: `TUI_REWORK.md` (dual-pane, M1ŌĆōM6) supersedes `TUI_DESIGN.md` ┬¦6 trigger-modal text inputs and the F3 free-text destination prompt.
    28	- Why: any field requiring the operator to recall and type an off-screen path is an interface failure.
    29	- Supersedes: TUI_DESIGN.md ┬¦6 (portions).
    30	
    31	## D-2026-06-04-1 ŌĆö R3 overrides R2 in the audit chain
    32	- Decision: where R2 and R3 disagree on a finding's severity or content, R3 wins; see the ID-override table in `AUDIT_REPORT_2026-06-04_INDEX.md`.
    33	- Why: R3 incorporates the GPT R2 critique and severity rebalance.
    34	- Supersedes: conflicting R2 entries.

    77	## D-2026-06-20-1 ŌĆö Transfer-core architecture conflict resolved: convergence, not ground-up redesign
    78	- Decision: The 2026-06-14 "redesign the transfer subsystem from the ground up" framing is resolved as **convergence**, not a rebuild. One src/dst-agnostic sequencer owns all four paths (localŌåölocal, push, pull, daemonŌåödaemon); the dial (stream count + all transfer knobs) is a single live object adjusted from measured telemetry; the already-shared byte-moving leaf stays. Dials are **bounded-unilateral** (receiver advertises a capacity ceiling; sender owns the dial within it) ~~and **size-gated** (small transfers skip the probe entirely)~~ **(size-gate framing superseded by D-2026-06-20-2 q1 ŌĆö there is no probe phase to skip; the engine moves within ~1s and tunes live)**. The adaptive-streams stack (PR1 telemetry + PR2 work-stealing queue, up to `eafb187`) is salvaged as the substrate per D-2026-06-07-2; PR3 WIP (`d9d4ec7`) stays excluded. ~~Built A-first (warmup), C-ready by construction (mutable dial + elastic stream-set exist from A, so continuous adjustment is a later feed, not a retrofit).~~ **(A/warmup staging superseded by D-2026-06-20-2 q1 ŌĆö conservative start + live tuning from the first byte; C shipped as `ue-r2-2` under REV4/D-2026-06-20-5.)** Plan: `docs/plan/UNIFIED_TRANSFER_ENGINE.md` (Draft ŌĆö awaiting owner DraftŌåÆActive flip). *(Stale wording struck 2026-07-04 on owner direction ŌĆö "follow the existing pattern": the in-place-annotation pattern of D-2026-06-20-3/-6. The convergence direction itself stands unchanged.)*
    79	- Why: owner (30-year IT veteran, not a developer) judges the fragmentation ŌĆö one engine for local, hand-wired loops for push/pull, three competing static stream-count tables, no live tuning ŌĆö is the root of the "localŌåölocal 10├Ś slower than localŌåÆdaemon" class of drift; a single engine makes that class impossible by construction and gives the LLM agent one place to update. Ground-up rebuild was judged too much; convergence on the existing shared leaf is the FAST/SIMPLE/RELIABLE fit. The adaptive substrate was purpose-built by an earlier Fable session as C's foundation, so building A on it does not paint the design into a corner.
    80	- Scope consequence: this **moots the standalone premise** of the queued incremental work and absorbs the goals ŌĆö w2-2 (three ladders ŌåÆ one dial) is `ue-1b`; w2-3 multi-stream pull (`MULTISTREAM_PULL.md`) is `ue-1d` via the unified sequencer; w2-4 (delete deprecated Pull RPC) is `ue-1e`; adaptive-streams cherry-pick is `ue-1a`. `MULTISTREAM_PULL.md` is superseded as a standalone plan (kept as reference); its goal survives inside this plan. The design-review queue's correctness findings (w4-1 etc.) are independent and unaffected.

    84	- Decision: `docs/plan/UNIFIED_TRANSFER_ENGINE.md` is **Active**.    104	## D-2026-06-20-6 ŌĆö CodeŌåÆGPT-reviewŌåÆfix loop for the unified engine; ungated per-slice commits
   105	- Decision: Adopt a synchronous codeŌåÆreviewŌåÆfix loop for the `ue-r2-*` slices (`docs/agent/GPT_REVIEW_LOOP.md`, Active). Claude codes + commits each slice, invokes GPT-5.5 via `codex` (headless here via the local `headroom` proxy) to review that commit, adjudicates every finding against source/tests, fixes the accepted ones, and proceeds. Three standing authorizations the owner gave this session: (a) **per-slice commits to `master` are ungated** for this loop ŌĆö no agent branches, never push (push stays owner-only); (b) **per-slice code-quality acceptance is delegated** to the loop + validation suite ŌĆö the owner is not a developer and will NOT be asked to bless code that passed validation+review ("that would just be theater"); (c) the agent proceeds autonomously and pauses only for genuine decisions/issues/blockers/plan-changes and the remaining owner gates (push; 10 GbE sign-off).
   106	- Why: the owner wants forward progress without rubber-stamp checkpoints. An external reviewer (GPT-5.5) catches what a single author misses, while Claude's adjudication guards against the reviewer's false positives ŌĆö demonstrated necessary the same day: a codex-class review's confident "two static tables, not three" claim was wrong (all three ladders are live). Commits are low-risk and reversible (nothing publishes until the owner pushes), so per-commit gating was pure friction.
   107	- Supersedes: nothing. ~~Scopes `.review/` usage for `ue-r2-*` only~~ **(scope clause superseded by D-2026-07-04-1 ŌĆö the loop is now repo-wide for all code and plan changes)** ŌĆö the async sentinel (`ready/`) + `reviewer-wait.sh` hand-off is not used (records `findings/` + `results/` are reused). Records the owner's explicit relaxation of the ┬¦9 per-slice-code checkpoint (code acceptance delegated to this loop); the ┬¦8 push gate and all other ┬¦9 owner gates stand.

   120	- Decision: The `CancelJob` dispatch policy stops refusing attached Push/PullSync jobs. /usr/bin/zsh -lc "nl -ba crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs | sed -n '1,80p'" in /home/michael/dev/Blit
 succeeded in 0ms:
     1	//! Retry-with-wait for transfers (owner-approved robocopy-style
     2	//! `--retry`/`--wait`). Part 1: the retryable-error classifier and the
     3	//! generic retry loop. Part 2 wires the CLI flags and the transfer
     4	//! dispatch through `run_with_retries`.
     5	//!
     6	//! This is viable because blit transfers are **resumable** ŌĆö a retry
     7	//! re-runs the same transfer, the manifest compare only re-sends
     8	//! missing/changed files, so a retry continues rather than restarts. The
     9	//! audit-1c stall-timeout is what turns an infinite stall into the clean,
    10	//! fast, retryable failure this loop catches.
    11	
    12	use std::future::Future;
    13	use std::time::Duration;
    14	
    15	use eyre::Result;
    16	
    17	// w5-2: the classifier moved to blit-core (single owner of retry
    18	// policy, next to the transfer code that produces the errors). The
    19	// re-export keeps this module's public API stable.
    20	pub use blit_core::remote::retry::is_retryable;
    21	
    22	/// Run `attempt` (a fresh transfer attempt; `attempt_no` is 0 on the
    23	/// first try) with up to `retries` retries spaced by `wait`. Retries fire
    24	/// only when [`is_retryable`] accepts the error; a fatal error returns
    25	/// immediately. `retries == 0` reproduces the no-retry default.
    26	///
    27	/// The transfer's resumability means each retry continues the prior
    28	/// attempt rather than restarting from scratch.
    29	pub async fn run_with_retries<F, Fut>(retries: u32, wait: Duration, mut attempt: F) -> Result<()>
    30	where
    31	    F: FnMut(u32) -> Fut,
    32	    Fut: Future<Output = Result<()>>,
    33	{
    34	    let mut attempt_no = 0u32;
    35	    loop {
    36	        match attempt(attempt_no).await {
    37	            Ok(()) => return Ok(()),
    38	            Err(err) => {
    39	                if attempt_no >= retries || !is_retryable(&err) {
    40	                    return Err(err);
    41	                }
    42	                attempt_no += 1;
    43	                eprintln!(
    44	                    "blit: transfer failed, retrying ({attempt_no}/{retries}) in {}s: {err:#}",
    45	                    wait.as_secs()
    46	                );
    47	                tokio::time::sleep(wait).await;
    48	            }
    49	        }
    50	    }
    51	}
    52	
    53	#[cfg(test)]
    54	mod tests {
    55	    use super::*;
    56	    use std::cell::Cell;
    57	    use std::io;
    58	
    59	    fn io_err(kind: io::ErrorKind) -> eyre::Report {
    60	        // Wrap in a context layer so the io::Error is a *source* in the
    61	        // chain, mirroring how the transfer code reports it.
    62	        eyre::Report::new(io::Error::new(kind, "boom")).wrap_err("receiving data")
    63	    }
    64	
    65	    #[test]
    66	    fn classifies_transient_io_as_retryable() {
    67	        assert!(is_retryable(&io_err(io::ErrorKind::TimedOut)));
    68	        assert!(is_retryable(&io_err(io::ErrorKind::ConnectionReset)));
    69	        assert!(is_retryable(&io_err(io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe)));
    70	        assert!(is_retryable(&io_err(io::ErrorKind::UnexpectedEof)));
    71	    }
    72	
    73	    #[test]
    74	    fn classifies_fatal_errors_as_not_retryable() {
    75	        // A plain eyre message (path-safety / gate / invalid-arg shape).
    76	        assert!(!is_retryable(&eyre::eyre!("path escapes module root")));
    77	        // An io error of a non-transient kind.
    78	        assert!(!is_retryable(&io_err(io::ErrorKind::PermissionDenied)));
    79	        assert!(!is_retryable(&io_err(io::ErrorKind::NotFound)));
    80	    }

Both are the same failure shape: one bad filename partway through a large localŌåÆremovable-media copy aborts the entire transfer instead of being skipped/reported. `audit-17`: the destination (a FAT-family filesystem on removable media, inferred from the hex volume label) rejects a `:` character in a NuGet http-cache path; `write_tar_shard_payload`'s `create_dir_all` (`sink.rs:605`) surfaces the raw `Invalid argument (os error 22)` and kills the run ŌĆö grepped the codebase for any existing invalid-filename handling and found none. `audit-18`: a non-UTF-8 source filename (valid on ext4) gets irreversibly mangled by `path_posix::relative_path_to_posix`'s per-component `to_string_lossy()` before any I/O is attempted; `build_tar_shard`'s `File::open` on the corrupted path 404s (`payload.rs:360`, `os error 2`) ŌĆö traced to the single shared helper both local mirror and remote push use (`engine/mirror.rs`, `mirror_planner.rs`, `remote/transfer/{payload,tar_safety}.rs`, `remote/endpoint.rs`, `remote/push/client/helpers.rs`), so it isn't a remote/proto-only issue, though a full remote-side fix is complicated by proto3 `string` being UTF-8-only on the wire. Both findings flag a needed owner design call (skip/report/sanitize/fail-fast policy) before any code ŌĆö filed, not fixed. Next: otp-7 (unrelated; continues per `docs/plan/OTP7_RESUME.md`).
